Corporate News: China Loan to Build In San Francisco Dies

Author: Whelan, Robbie

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 12 Apr 2013: B.3.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/corporate-news-china-loan-build-san-francisco/docview/1326087327/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: U.S. home builder Lennar Corp. had been in talks with the China Development Bank for more than a year about a loan to finance some 20,000 new homes and millions of square feet of commercial space on the site of two former naval bases, Treasure Island and Hunters Point Shipyard.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Corporate+News%3A+China+Loan+to+Build+In+San+Francisco+Dies&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-12&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=B.3&amp;au=Whelan%2C+Robbie&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   A closely watched deal under which a state-run Chinese bank would have provided $1.7 billion for two huge housing developments in San Francisco collapsed after changes in bank leadership and U.S. tax laws complicated negotiations, according to a person familiar with the talks.
U.S. home builder Lennar Corp. had been in talks with the China Development Bank for more than a year about a loan to finance some 20,000 new homes and millions of square feet of commercial space on the site of two former naval bases, Treasure Island and Hunters Point Shipyard.
In December, a bank committee approved the loan, which required Lennar to work on the project with China Railway Construction Corp., a state-run contractor. China Railway's role was never made clear, but the company opened an office in San Mateo, Calif., and had been meeting with local construction officials.
China Development Bank officials didn't immediately respond to a request for comment.
Lennar and the bank had been trying to close the loan to avoid potential costs arising from the Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act, which requires foreign banks to disclose certain data about American account holders or be subject to a 30% tax on income from their U.S.-held assets.
Another issue causing delay was the potential for a shift in China Development Bank's leadership. The bank's chairman, Chen Yuan, at 68 years old, is past retirement age.
Miami-based Lennar Corp., the third-largest U.S. home builder, was picked in 1999 to develop Hunters Point, a shipbuilding site in World War II. Its plan calls for 12,500 homes, a hotel, 3.5 million square feet of research-development and commercial space and 800,000 square feet of retail space.
On Treasure Island, a man-made island in the middle of San Francisco Bay, Lennar is partnering with several local developers and private-equity firms to build up to 8,000 homes, a hotel and commercial space.
Both developments had struck agreements with local trade unions to use local labor to build the houses and commercial properties. Tim Paulson, executive director of the San Francisco Labor Council, said last month that talks between Lennar and the Chinese seemed to be taking a long time.
San Francisco Mayor Ed Lee visited China from late March until April 7 to promote the city's relationship with China. Local news reports before he left suggested he planned to discuss the Treasure Island and San Francisco projects with Chinese bank officials. Mr. Lee's office didn't immediately respond to requests for comment.
News the deal had collapsed was first reported on the web site of the San Francisco Chronicle.
The collapse of the talks with China Development Bank raises questions about the projects' future. Lennar has begun construction of the Hunters Point project but will need to come up with another financing source to pay for the bulk of both projects.
"We are continuing to move forward with development of Hunters Point Shipyard and are expecting to start home construction this summer," a Lennar spokesman said. "At the same time, lenders continue to have significant interest in financing the Shipyard and Treasure Island, which they believe are extremely attractive projects."

World News: Doubt Over Export Numbers Colors China's Trade Report

Author: Silk, Richard

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 11 Apr 2013: A.12.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-doubt-over-export-numbers-colors/docview/1325314728/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: Economists raised fresh doubts about China's export data after figures for March showed a surprise trade deficit, with some suggesting the performance of the country's crucial export sector might have been weaker than it appeared.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+Doubt+Over+Export+Numbers+Colors+China%27s+Trade+Report&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-11&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.12&amp;au=Silk%2C+Richard&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   BEIJING -- Economists raised fresh doubts about China's export data after figures for March showed a surprise trade deficit, with some suggesting the performance of the country's crucial export sector might have been weaker than it appeared.
A number of economists have questioned a surge in Chinese exports in recent months despite continued slow growth in regions that purchase Chinese exports and the Chinese currency's appreciation. They say the figures have likely been inflated by those trying to skirt China's capital controls and bring hot money into the country to take advantage of the strengthening yuan.
If demand for China's exports is partly a mirage, as these economists suggest, it not only means expectations for China's own recovery may have to be tamped down: China's strong performance in the last quarter had fueled hopes about a pickup in global demand.
The strict limits on the amounts of money that can be either taken into or out of China have fostered a variety of strategies to skirt them. Two businesses or individuals could agree to exaggerate or understate the value of a transaction in deals that can serve both outsiders eager to get capital into China for investment purposes and those based on the mainland who want to move some of their money out.
After reporting strong trade surpluses since December, China said Wednesday it swung to an $884 million trade deficit amid higher imports and slower export growth. In February, China posted a $15.25 billion surplus.
Exports rose 10% year to year in March, down from February's dramatic 21.8% rise. Still, some economists remained skeptical.
"This 10% export growth is more real as it's in line with other data such as power consumption, industrial production and transportation," said Bank of AmericaMerrill Lynch economist Lu Ting in a research note. "That said, even the 10% reading in March might be overreported."
IHS Global Insight economists Xianfang Ren and Alistair Thornton called "astounding" a 93% year-to-year rise in March exports to Hong Kong -- where many exporters have close cultural and financial ties.
"The breakdown of exports by destination veers towards the absurd," they said in a note. By contrast, March exports to the U.S. and the European Union were down 6.5% and 14% respectively from a year earlier.
A spokesman for China's customs administration said Wednesday that the authority is investigating allegations of falsified data. "We will certainly take action if needed," Zheng Yuesheng said at a briefing on the trade figures.
Citing exporters, The Wall Street Journal reported last week that it has become common practice for some companies to overreport the value of exported goods. That results in bigger profits for exporters if the local currency rises in value. The yuan has advanced only about 0.6% against the dollar so far this year but a recovering economy could spell further gains ahead.
Exporters could also be falsifying documents to illegally claim tax rebates on their outbound shipments, according to people familiar with these trade practices. They also said some local governments claim higher export numbers to look good.
Though China typically runs a large trade surplus with the rest of the world, it isn't unusual for it to post a deficit in individual months. Trade figures have also been complicated by the Lunar New Year holiday, in February this year and January last year. Imports fell in February, likely due to the holiday, when much industrial activity slows.
---
Yajun Zhang contributed to this article.

Full text:   CHINA
Banks Boosted Lending
Sharply in March, Data Show
China saw a large increase in lending in March, data released Thursday showed, reawakening concerns over inflation in the world's second-largest economy.
Banks made 1.06 trillion Chinese yuan ($171 billion) of net new loans, up from 620 billon yuan in February and well above expectations, despite pressure from the central bank to hold the line on lending.
While the growth of credit suggests strong economic momentum in China, it also raises concerns among economists of a resurgence in inflation and the prospect of asset bubbles, particularly in the real-estate market.
Consumer inflation fell back to 2.1% in March, after a holiday-induced spike in February, but economists warn that the latest lending figures suggest problems ahead.
-- Richard Silk
Former Rail Minister
Is Charged With Bribery
Prosecutors charged China's former railway chief with bribery and abuse of power, state media said, moving closer to trial the case of a once-powerful official who came to represent China's pervasive government corruption.
The official Xinhua news agency said that the Beijing No. 2 Intermediate People's Court accepted a criminal indictment against Liu Zhijun. This paves the way for a civilian trial of the former minister at an unspecified later date. Mr. Liu's whereabouts isn't clear. He has made no public statements or appearances since being fired in early 2011.
-- James T. Areddy
---
YEMEN
President Overhauls
Leadership of Military
Yemen's president removed his predecessor's son and nephews from powerful security posts in the most dramatic step yet in sidelining old regime figures, according to the nation's state-run media.
Ex-President Ali Abdullah Saleh, who stepped down in 2012, placed relatives and loyalists into top military and government posts over his 33-year rule. His vice president, Abed Rabbo Mansour Hadi, took over in a deal brokered by Yemen's Gulf neighbors and backed by the U.S.
-- Associated Press
---
SOMALIA
Piracy Declines Sharply
Piracy off Somalia's coast pushes up global trade costs by $18 billion a year, the World Bank said, but behind that figure is a sharp decline in recent attacks, bringing some relief to the East African nation.
In a report released Thursday, the bank said piracy amounted to a "hidden tax" on seaborne trade and a deep blow to the economies of both Somalia and its more stable neighbors. Still, attacks fell from a peak of 160 in 2011 to 49 last year, the International Maritime Bureau said.
-- Patrick McGroarty
---
MALAYSIA
Date of General Election Set
Malaysia set May 5 to hold what could be its closest general elections ever, pitting the National Front coalition and its decadeslong rule amid strong economic growth against the opposition and its pledge to boost living standards and create a corruption-free government.
The Election Commission said Wednesday that candidates will be nominated on April 20, kicking off a two-week campaign period that will send 222 lawmakers to Parliament. Last week, Prime Minister Najib Razak dissolved Parliament to make way for the election.
-- Abhrajit Gangopadhyay

Corn Prices Rise on Report

Author: Fletcher, Owen; Tomson, Bill

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 11 Apr 2013: C.4.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/corn-prices-rise-on-report/docview/1325303631/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: Corn prices rose after the U.S. Department of Agriculture forecast tighter-than-expected domestic supplies of the grain.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Corn+Prices+Rise+on+Report&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-11&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=C.4&amp;au=Fletcher%2C+Owen%3BTomson%2C+Bill&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   CHICAGO -- Corn prices rose after the U.S. Department of Agriculture forecast tighter-than-expected domestic supplies of the grain.
In the monthly crop report, the USDA raised its projection for supplies before this fall's harvest by 20%, to 757 million bushels. The forecast surprised some traders because analysts had projected a jump of 30%, on average, in a Dow Jones Newswires survey.
The government elevated its forecast for supplies on Aug. 31, the end of the current crop year, because it expects lower demand for corn from livestock companies and foreign importers. However, the USDA raised its projection for how much corn will be consumed by the ethanol industry.
Corn for May delivery gained 4.75 cents, or 0.7%, to settle at $6.49 a bushel at the Chicago Board of Trade.
Corn prices fell earlier in the trading session because the USDA's forecast for global corn supplies was higher than analysts had expected. The USDA projected that global corn supplies will total 125.3 million metric tons this year, well above analysts' expectations. The agency raised its estimate primarily because of decreased demand for corn in animal feed in the U.S., as well as in China and Mexico.
"There's something for both the bulls and the bears out there today," said Chad Henderson, president of Prime-Ag Consultants Inc., a commodity brokerage in Brookfield, Wis. "At the end of the day today, the bulls won by a nickel."
Wheat and soybean prices fell Wednesday, as the USDA forecast significantly greater-than-expected world supplies of the two commodities.
CBOT May wheat settled down 12 cents, or 1.7%, at $6.9675 a bushel. May soybeans fell 2.75 cents, or 0.2%, to $13.9275 a bushel.
---
Ian Berry contributed to this article.

World News: U.S. Seeks Less Austerity in Euro Zone

Author: Catan, Thomas

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 10 Apr 2013: A.8.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-u-s-seeks-less-austerity-euro-zone/docview/1324941650/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: Later, in Paris, his last stop before returning to Washington, Mr. Lew got more backing for the U.S. position from the French finance minister, Pierre Moscovici, who stressed the need for euro members to "maintain a balanced approach between repairing public finances and doing whatever necessary to ensure an economic pickup in the euro zone."

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+U.S.+Seeks+Less+Austerity+in+Euro+Zone&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-10&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.8&amp;au=Catan%2C+Thomas&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   BERLIN -- U.S. Treasury Secretary Jacob Lew's whirlwind trip to Europe this week ended Tuesday, underscoring the stark trans-Atlantic divide over how best to recover from the global economic slump.
At four stops over two days, Mr. Lew pressed the Obama administration's view that Europe should go slower on its German-led austerity drive to avoid snuffing out the recovery. He also called on Germany to enact policies to boost consumer spending and on businesses to help revive growth.
"Global demand needs to grow," Mr. Lew said following his meeting here with his German counterpart. "Policies that would help to encourage consumer demand in countries that have the capacity would be helpful."
Many European governments are cutting spending and raising taxes to shrink budget deficits that ballooned after the financial crisis. Some, such as Greece and Portugal, have no choice under terms of international bailout agreements. Others, such as the U.K. and Germany, say they must pursue balanced budgets to ensure confidence in their public finances and stronger long-run growth.
The Obama administration and the International Monetary Fund have warned that the efforts, if pursued too rapidly, could be self-defeating by restraining growth, which could widen deficits and make government debts harder to pay. The outcome matters to the U.S. because its economy is closely linked to Europe's and could be hurt if the euro zone's financial turmoil escalates.
Mr. Lew, on his second official trip abroad after one to China, hinted on Tuesday that Europe should ease the pace of its austerity efforts until growth picks up, pointing to the improving economic picture in the U.S. The U.S. economy has expanded for more than three years, while growth in the euro zone is about zero. The U.S. has sought to "balance growth and fiscal discipline in a way that keeps our recovery strong," he said. "It has meant some midcourse corrections and extending the period of fiscal consolidation."
But Germany's finance minister, Wolfgang Schauble, seemed unconvinced by the U.S. arguments.
"Nobody in Europe sees this contradiction between fiscal-policy consolidation and growth," said Mr. Schauble. "We have a growth-friendly process of consolidation."
U.S. officials say they see signs Europe is starting to make growth a bigger priority, partly because of the region's rising unemployment rate. The jobless rate in the 17-nation euro area has hit a record 12%, but some individual members, such as Spain and Greece, are suffering more than twice that rate.
At a news conference with Mr. Schauble, Mr. Lew said pointedly that deficit reduction needed to be balanced with growth and investment policies. While growth targets may differ for different countries, he said, "I think it is fair to say that zero isn't a good target for anybody and negative is very bad."
Later, in Paris, his last stop before returning to Washington, Mr. Lew got more backing for the U.S. position from the French finance minister, Pierre Moscovici, who stressed the need for euro members to "maintain a balanced approach between repairing public finances and doing whatever necessary to ensure an economic pickup in the euro zone."
During his trip, Mr. Lew also pressed a range of other priorities of the U.S., including its view that Europe must urgently move to a system of regionwide banking supervision to prevent further banking crises, as well as coming negotiations over a trans-Atlantic free-trade pact.
---
Gabriele Parussini in Paris contributed to this article.

China Lets 170 Auto Makers Bloom --- Local Government Incentives Keep Small Companies Expanding Even as Beijing Tries to Encourage Industry Consolidation

Author: Anonymous

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 10 Apr 2013: B.10.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/china-lets-170-auto-makers-bloom-local-government/docview/1324932853/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: According to research firm IHS, a company called Tianqi Meiya sold 77 passenger cars last year. According to a plan the city issued in 2010, officials committed to giving local auto makers land and helping them recruit talent, and it allowed banks to roll over loans to cash-strapped companies.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=China+Lets+170+Auto+Makers+Bloom+---+Local+Government+Incentives+Keep+Small+Companies+Expanding+Even+as+Beijing+Tries+to+Encourage+Industry+Consolidation&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-10&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=B.10&amp;au=Anonymous&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   TAIZHOU, China -- The U.S. auto industry has long had three big domestic car makers. China has more than 170, including tiny Zhejiang Jonway Automobile Co.
Jonway makes a sport-utility vehicle named after the Airbus A380 jumbo jet. Its A380 SUV starts at 70,000 yuan ($11,272) and is marketed as a smooth, low-maintenance ride.
Customers aren't buying it. Last year Jonway sold about 5,000 cars compared with the more than 7,000 that Volkswagen AG sells on average in China every day.
Little Jonway isn't fazed by the market reception. It plans to release a new SUV model this year, beef up marketing and is considering exporting vehicles to South America. It continues to work on its technology with the help of supportive local officials, and it just received a license from the Chinese government to begin making electric cars.
"China is the largest car market in the world, and it still has potential to grow. Our ambitions are congruent with reality," insists Alex Wang, Jonway's 31-year-old, U.K.-educated chairman.
Optimistic Chinese auto executives like Mr. Wang send shudders through the rest of the global auto sector. Industry watchers worry that the world's No. 1 auto market could soon be awash in overcapacity. That would rev up competition in China and pressure companies here to export more of their cars.
"We may see high levels of overcapacity and significant margin pressure within the next three to five years," said Bill Russo, president of auto consulting firm Synergistics Ltd. and a former Chrysler executive. He estimates that China's overcapacity in three years could total 10 million cars, roughly equivalent to Japan's 2012 auto production.
Overcapacity worries aren't confined to cars. China has a glut of factories in industries ranging from steel to construction equipment to solar panels. Beijing encouraged heavy investment in those industries to move away from its dependence on low-level manufacturing. While central government officials signal that they want to tamp down on capacity, local governments are still backing local champions that are major employers.
China's car-making capacity is set to soar in coming years. General Motors Co., Volkswagen and Ford Motor Co. are building new factories and assembly lines. China's top 10 auto groups -- which make both foreign and domestic brands -- are expected to have combined capacity to build about 35 million vehicles a year by the end of 2015, according to their previous announcements, compared with 18 million vehicles in 2012.
But sales growth is slowing. McKinsey & Co. forecasts that China's auto market will grow by an average 8% a year through 2020, down from a compound average rate of 24% between 2005 and 2011.
Experts expect domestic brands will incur the brunt of the slower gains because foreign brands such as GM and VW enjoy a reputation for quality among Chinese drivers. Foreign brands currently make up roughly two-thirds of China passenger car sales. Last year, Dong Yang, vice chairman of the semiofficial China Association of Automobile Manufacturers predicted about half of domestic brands may disappear in coming years.
But many Chinese companies enjoy subsidies designed to bolster local champions. For example, the western city of Chongqing said last June it would give a subsidy of up to 3,000 yuan for buyers of some models of vans made by local car maker Chongqing Changan Automobile Co., while FAW Car Co. said in August that the northeastern city of Changchun would offer a subsidy of between 3,500 yuan and 7,000 yuan for buyers of some cars made by the company. The U.S. last year filed a case before the World Trade Organization arguing that China unfairly supports auto companies and parts makers, an accusation Beijing disputes.
Many are also looking abroad. Last year Chinese auto exports rose 19% to one million vehicles, mainly to markets in the Middle East, Russia, and South America, according to the trade association.
Chinese officials have acknowledged the problem. In July, the Ministry of Industry and Information Technology said China has more than 171 car, truck and bus manufacturers, and said passenger vehicle producers that make fewer than 1,000 vehicles for two years in a row will be ordered to overhaul production.
China has auto makers even smaller than Jonway. According to research firm IHS, a company called Tianqi Meiya sold 77 passenger cars last year. The company, in the north Chinese city of Tianjin, didn't respond to requests for comment.
Jonway builds its vehicles in Taizhou, an eastern city where local officials are pushing to create their China's version of Detroit. According to a plan the city issued in 2010, officials committed to giving local auto makers land and helping them recruit talent, and it allowed banks to roll over loans to cash-strapped companies.
Other auto companies doing business in the region include Zhejiang Geely Holding Group Co., the Chinese auto maker which acquired Volvo Car Corp. from Ford Motor Co. in 2010.
Jonway's U.S. parent, a Santa Rosa, Calif., electric vehicle company called Zap, said in its most recent annual securities filing that the Chinese auto company received $1.6 million in subsidies and incentives in 2010 and 2011 combined. Jonway reported a 2011 loss of $10.2 million on sales of $54.3 million.
Mr. Wang's father and Jonway's founder, Wang Huaiyi, is a major Zap shareholder and a member of the board. The Wang family started its China-based business in the early 1980s, producing everything from buttons for clothes to parts of electric fans. In the 1990s it began supplying parts for motorcycles made by Geely before the latter began making cars.
Inspired by the high-profile success of Geely Chairman Li Shufu, in 2003 the senior Mr. Wang invested 600 million yuan, or about $72 million, in an SUV manufacturing facility with an aim at targeting China's growing middle class.
The younger Mr. Wang began managing Jonway in 2008 two years after returning from studying in the U.K. "I've never thought of the overcapacity problem," he said. Jonway "has done very well in the motorcycle business and it needs a bigger platform to grow. The car industry is just the platform through which we can grow stronger."
Jonway used Toyota Motor Corp.'s RAV4 SUV as a reference when designing the five-door A380, he said. Its sales grew to nearly 8,000 in 2010 from 4,500 the year before.
But sales began slumping in 2011 with China's decision to end buyers subsidies for cars with engine capacity of 1.6 liters or smaller. Mr. Wang said he believes the sales problem is marketing.
"Building brand recognition needs time," he said. "Jonway is in urgent need of improved marketing."
Jonway aims to sell 20,000 SUVs and minivans this year, and plans to add 50 dealers to its existing network of 100 dealers across the country. Other efforts include bigger dealer incentives, more advertising spending and a push to raise its profile at this month's auto show in Shanghai, he said.
It is also eyeing exports, targeting volume of 3,000 vehicles in emerging markets such as South America and Africa, Mr. Wang said. Jonway parent Zap has a team of Spanish-speaking sales representatives, "which is a unique edge to us."
-- Rose Yu

Aussie, Yuan to Be Convertible

Author: Curran, Enda

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 09 Apr 2013: C.4.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/aussie-yuan-be-convertible/docview/1324533302/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: The Australian prime minister, on a five-day visit to China that began Friday, said the People's Bank of China already had approved licenses for Westpac Banking Corp. and Australia & New Zealand Banking Group Ltd. to act as market makers for direct trading of the currencies.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Aussie%2C+Yuan+to+Be+Convertible&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-09&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=C.4&amp;au=Curran%2C+Enda&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   SYDNEY -- Australia and China agreed to allow each other's currencies to be directly converted, Australian Prime Minister Julia Gillard said Monday. Starting Wednesday, the Australian dollar will be convertible into the yuan and vice versa.
Australia will be the third country to have such an arrangement, which is expected to cut costs for local companies doing business in China, Australia's biggest trading partner. Only the U.S. dollar and Japanese yen are directly exchangeable with the yuan.
The agreement eliminates the need for companies and currency traders to first convert their Australian dollars or yuan into U.S. dollars.
"This is a huge advantage for Australia," Ms. Gillard told reporters in Shanghai, flanked by executives from some of Australia's biggest banks. "It's a strategic step forward for Australia as we add to our economic engagement with China."
The Australian prime minister, on a five-day visit to China that began Friday, said the People's Bank of China already had approved licenses for Westpac Banking Corp. and Australia & New Zealand Banking Group Ltd. to act as market makers for direct trading of the currencies.
"This takes costs out and makes it a whole lot more convenient," Gail Kelly, chief executive of Westpac, said at the news conference. Several major Chinese banks also are expected to be appointed as market makers, said a person familiar with the matter.
China introduced a yuan/Australian dollar exchange rate to its onshore currency market in November 2011, but trading of the pair has been done indirectly through the U.S. dollar. Some analysts said the new agreement would take time to change the shape of currency transactions between the two countries. Australia's exports to China are mostly bulk commodities, including iron ore and coal, priced in U.S. dollars. Few expect that arrangement to be altered soon.
Australian businesses have been slow to embrace the yuan, but that may be changing. Local companies sharply increased their use of China's currency for global trade payments late last year, according to the Society for Worldwide Interbank Financial Telecommunication, a global payments system.
Mike Smith, chief executive of ANZ, expects trading volumes to rise as a result of the new two-way agreement.
"It will become a proper traded currency mix and the volumes of that are limitless," Mr. Smith said at the news conference.
The close economic relationship with China has helped shield Australia from the turmoil in Europe and the fragility of the U.S. recovery. About 20% of the nation's exports go to China, with two-way goods-and-services trade between the countries valued at 128 billion Australian dollars ($133 billion) for the 2011-12 financial year.
Ms. Gillard's government has advocated a freer exchange-rate policy in China, arguing that such a move is vital to balancing global growth. Recent talks between the nations have been aimed at boosting yuan-denominated trade.
For its part, Beijing is slowly working to liberalize the yuan. In 2012, it allowed the currency to move within a wider daily range against the U.S. dollar.
---
Wynne Wang in Shanghai contributed to this article.

World News: Putin Shrugs Off Criticism in Germany of Rights Record

Author: Boston, William; Lange, Stefan

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 09 Apr 2013: A.10.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-putin-shrugs-off-criticism-germany/docview/1324530763/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: German politicians and human-rights activists attacked what they called Moscow's repression of civic groups, its attitude toward gays and its support for Syrian leader Bashar al-Assad in that country's bloody civil war.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+Putin+Shrugs+Off+Criticism+in+Germany+of+Rights+Record&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-09&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.10&amp;au=Boston%2C+William%3BLange%2C+Stefan&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   HANNOVER, Germany -- Russian President Vladimir Putin and German Chancellor Angela Merkel dodged topless protesters and traded barbs over civil rights but largely stuck to business during a visit to a trade fair Monday.
Political disruptions were hard to avoid, even in the run-up to Mr. Putin's high-profile appearance at the annual Hannover Industry Trade Fair. German politicians and human-rights activists attacked what they called Moscow's repression of civic groups, its attitude toward gays and its support for Syrian leader Bashar al-Assad in that country's bloody civil war.
When the Russian and German leaders strolled through the spacious halls of the trade fair Monday, the protests became more tangible.
Three women charged the pair, ripping off their blazers to expose their breasts and profanities and the name of the punk band Pussy Riot written in black paint on their skin. The women were close enough to touch Mr. Putin before Russian security guards jumped into the fray and wrestled the protesters away.
Such protests, initiated by the Ukrainian group Femen, have become common wherever Mr. Putin appears. "We're used to these actions and I don't see anything terrible in them," he said. "If someone wants to have a discussion on some political issues then it's better to do it while you are dressed, and not take your clothes off."
While Mr. Putin laughed off the incident, worries about the erosion of democratic rights are no joke for the Germans. Ms. Merkel publicly reproached Mr. Putin for the treatment of German nongovernmental organizations in Russia, once in a speech Sunday before Germany's industrial elite and again at a news conference on Monday.
"It is important that an NGO can work well and free," Ms. Merkel said. Confiscating computer drives is a "disruption and intervention" of this work, she added. "A vibrant civil society can only emerge if individual organizations are able to operate without fear and worry."
Mr. Putin gave no ground to Ms. Merkel's pressure. He defended the wave of official audits of civil society groups over the past month or so as routine and part of Kremlin efforts to implement new laws that he said mirrored U.S. and European ones.
Analysts say one such Russian law, which requires any group that engages in anything seen as political activity to register as a "foreign agent," is much broader than Western analogs.
It is hard to imagine such a chilly greeting for a Russian leader under past German chancellors. Helmut Kohl enjoyed a warm relationship with President Boris Yeltsin. And Gerhard Schroder is still so close to Mr. Putin that he invited the Russian leader to his birthday party on Sunday evening.
Raised in Soviet-dominated East Germany as the daughter of a Lutheran pastor, Ms. Merkel has transformed Germany's relationship to Russia, putting it on a more businesslike footing. Much the way that Germany views China as a huge economic opportunity, Ms. Merkel stresses business rather than cultural ties to Russia.
"Putin and Merkel don't share a close personal relationship. They both know that the relationship is important, that business is the foundation of German-Russian relations," said Stefan Meister, an expert on Russia and Eastern Europe at the German Council on Foreign Relations. "The rhetoric in Germany's discussion of Russia has changed."
The question is whether Germany and Russia will go back to their old ways if Ms. Merkel is ousted from power in September's election. Her Social Democrat challenger, Peer Steinbruck, suggested recently that the West shouldn't impose its principles of pluralistic democracy on Russia.
But analysts think Germany may have soured on Mr. Putin's brand of strongman politics.
"There may not be a way back," said Mr. Meister. "There is a new fundamental debate about Russia in Germany today."

What's Ahead -- People & Events To Watch In The Coming Week

Author: Anonymous

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 08 Apr 2013: A.1.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/whats-ahead-people-events-watch-coming-week/docview/1324451369/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: None available.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

Soybeans Hit by China's Bird-Flu Outbreak, U.S. Supplies

Author: Berry, Ian

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 06 Apr 2013: B.5.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/soybeans-hit-chinas-bird-flu-outbreak-u-s/docview/1324251899/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: The USDA report, along with sharp declines in corn futures and the emergence of the bird-flu outbreak, have led speculators such as hedge funds to exit from bets on rising soybean prices as they brace for more losses, analysts said Friday.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Soybeans+Hit+by+China%27s+Bird-Flu+Outbreak%2C+U.S.+Supplies&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-06&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=B.5&amp;au=Berry%2C+Ian&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   U.S. soybean prices slumped to a fresh 10-month low amid fears that export demand for the oilseed will slow due to a bird-flu outbreak in China.
Traders worry the outbreak will lead to reduced poultry consumption in China and prompt producers to cull their flocks to prevent the spread of the new bird-flu strain.
A cutback in chicken production would result in lower demand for soybean meal, a widely used ingredient in chicken feed. Chinese state media reported Friday that six people have died after being infected with the H7N9 virus.
The outbreak comes as Chinese soybean imports already have been slowing and trail forecasts by the U.S. Department of Agriculture, analysts said. China is the world's largest soybean importer, accounting for about 60% of imports, and its purchases have a huge impact on prices.
Soybean futures for May delivery fell 10.25 cents, or 0.8%, to $13.6175 a bushel Friday at the Chicago Board of Trade. That marked the lowest closing price for the front-month contract since June 5, 2012.
Soybean prices have dropped 6% since the USDA reported March 28 that U.S. supplies of soybeans, corn and wheat as of March 1 were all higher than analysts had expected.
The USDA report, along with sharp declines in corn futures and the emergence of the bird-flu outbreak, have led speculators such as hedge funds to exit from bets on rising soybean prices as they brace for more losses, analysts said Friday. Corn and soybean prices often move in tandem, as the crops are planted on the same ground across the U.S. Midwest and both are used in animal feed.
Analysts said the soybean market may remain under pressure as long as the weather is favorable for farmers, who are preparing to plant their crops in coming weeks.
"This is a liquidating market until we run into a crop problem," said Rich Feltes, vice president of research for R.J. O'Brien & Associates LLC in Chicago.
Traders expect U.S. farmers to dedicate more acreage to soybeans this year. Some say a chilly start to the spring may lead to even more plantings as farmers who had intended to grow corn switch to soybeans, which have a later growing season.

World News: Concerns Grow About New Avian-Flu Strain --- Disease May Move Easily to Humans; U.S. Is Preparing to Develop a Vaccine

Author: Chin, Josh; McKay, Betsy

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 06 Apr 2013: A.6.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-concerns-grow-about-new-avian-flu/docview/1324249601/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: The U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention warned U.S. public-health departments and physicians to be on the lookout for signs of the new virus, a variant of the H7N9 strain of avian flu.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+Concerns+Grow+About+New+Avian-Flu+Strain+---+Disease+May+Move+Easily+to+Humans%3B+U.S.+Is+Preparing+to+Develop+a+Vaccine&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-06&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.6&amp;au=Chin%2C+Josh%3BMcKay%2C+Betsy&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   BEIJING -- Concerns about a deadly new strain of bird flu intensified Friday as the disease claimed a sixth life in eastern China and agricultural authorities in Shanghai ordered a wide-scale slaughter of poultry in an effort to stem its spread.
The U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention warned U.S. public-health departments and physicians to be on the lookout for signs of the new virus, a variant of the H7N9 strain of avian flu. The CDC said it is developing a diagnostic kit to send to U.S. states and China, and is working on a seed virus for a vaccine that could be prepared should the disease start spreading human-to-human.
Flu experts said they are concerned about the new virus because it exhibits signs of being more readily able to infect humans from ailing birds than is another form of avian flu known as H5N1, which has been infecting people off and on for more than a decade.
China now has confirmed 16 cases of H7N9 nationwide, with patients ranging in age from 4 to 87, who became ill between Feb. 19 and March 31. The number of cases, while small, is large for the early stages of an outbreak, and some flu experts said the fact that they are spread over a relatively wide geographic area is reason for concern.
Among the people found to be infected, several are believed to have been in close contact with birds, including a 48-year-old who transported poultry, a 45-year-old poultry butcher and a 38-year-old chef.
Authorities stressed they have yet to find a case of human-to-human transmission, which would make the disease more dangerous; the cases they have seen appear to come from human contact with birds.
"So far there is no evidence that the H7N9 virus can be spread between human beings, which makes us relieved," Wu Fan, director of the Shanghai Center for Disease Control and Prevention, said Friday.
Chinese authorities are investigating illnesses in the families of two of the people who had confirmed H7N9, to see if any members have the disease -- a finding that could suggest human transmission.
Still, "the fact that we haven't seen cases in contacts and haven't seen it widespread in children" and elsewhere "are all reassuring," said U.S. CDC Director Thomas Frieden. The U.S. agency has worked closely with Chinese public-health authorities to improve the country's flu surveillance and lab testing in recent years, and Dr. Frieden said he had a "long conversation" Thursday night with his counterpart on the evolving situation.
No cases have been identified in the U.S. "There are no specific steps people in this country need to take to protect themselves," Dr. Frieden said.
Worries the new bird-flu strain in China will stifle air travel sent shares of the nation's airlines falling sharply, triggering a broader selloff in airline and travel stocks world-wide. Chinese flag carrier Air China Ltd. fell 9.8%, its biggest one-day decline since April 27, 2009.
Other governments in the region have made efforts to contain the disease. Hong Kong and Taiwan are stepping up temperature checks in airports, using sensors that screen passengers as they pass through a gate.
The world has become more than familiar over the past decade with avian flu, which typically circulates in birds and can jump to humans. The emergence and spread of H5N1 avian flu more than a decade ago prompted countries such as the U.S. to develop elaborate and expensive pandemic preparedness plans. H5N1 proved frighteningly deadly -- killing 60% of those it infected -- but despite infecting 622 people in 15 countries, it hasn't spread readily from one human to another.
Whether this new H7N9 flu, a different avian-flu strain, is deadlier than H5N1 isn't yet clear, because it isn't yet known how many people have been infected or how sick they are. Still, the new H7N9 is more worrying than H5N1 in some ways. Genetic changes in the avian virus suggest it may be adapting to infect mammals, said Nancy Cox, a virologist who is the CDC's Atlanta-based flu chief.
But she cautioned that little is still known about the new virus. The CDC hopes to receive a virus isolate or isolates from China within the next week or so, she said, and will study the genetic changes further to try to determine how transmissible the virus may be among humans.
Another challenge is that unlike H5N1, which can kill birds, this H7N9 virus doesn't make birds very ill -- so there is little sign it is spreading in flocks.
The appearance of the new virus has shaken China, where memories of the crippling 2003 outbreak of severe acute respiratory syndrome remain fresh. Unlike with SARS, the government has vowed to be transparent and release information as quickly as possible, though many in China remain skeptical.
China's state media and local governments have flooded social-media sites with information about H7N9, which scientists say may be susceptible to the two most powerful antiviral drugs, Tamiflu and Relenza.
Shanghai authorities moved Friday to destroy thousands of birds, ordering the closure of wholesale poultry markets and instructing vendors in smaller markets to immediately cull their chicken populations.
The U.S. Consulate in Shanghai issued a statement Friday urging people to remain calm. "At this point the risk for international disease spread is considered low," the consulate said. "The latest advisory from the World Health Organization as of April 4 is that no travel or trade restrictions with China should be applied based on the current information."
---
James T. Areddy in Shanghai, Jeffrey Ng in Hong Kong and Aries Poon in Taipei contributed to this article.

World News: Doubts Cast on Chinese Exports

Author: Anonymous

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 04 Apr 2013: A.9.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-doubts-cast-on-chinese-exports/docview/1323771047/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: A discrepancy between China's export data and Hong Kong import numbers is raising doubts about what appeared to be booming overseas demand for Chinese goods, amid uncertainty about the strength of the recovery in the world's second-largest economy.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+Doubts+Cast+on+Chinese+Exports&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-04&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.9&amp;au=Anonymous&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   BEIJING -- A discrepancy between China's export data and Hong Kong import numbers is raising doubts about what appeared to be booming overseas demand for Chinese goods, amid uncertainty about the strength of the recovery in the world's second-largest economy.
China's customs bureau reported in March that exports rose 19.8% year-to-year in the three months through February, despite a fragile recovery in the U.S. and Europe. The report has buoyed confidence that China's economy is strengthening, after growth in gross domestic product touched a three-year low of 7.4% year-to-year in the third quarter of 2012.
But some exporters, trade agents and economists said the export numbers were likely to be inaccurate because of false reporting by exporters and local governments. They point in particular to mismatching trade figures with Hong Kong, the first destination for many mainland Chinese goods.
In the three months through February, mainland customs reported $94.9 billion in exports to Hong Kong, but Hong Kong customs reported only $58.7 billion in imports from the mainland. The discrepancy during the period was greater than at any other time in recent years.
China's export growth for February could have been overstated by around seven percentage points, based on an analysis of data discrepancies, Louis Kuijs, China economist at RBS, estimated.
Some exporters exaggerate invoices to gain tax rebates and evade controls on bringing cash into the country, and some local governments claim higher export numbers to look good, people familiar with reporting practices said. "Fake exporting is rampant," said an export-agency owner in Foshan, in southern Guangdong province.
"It's really easy to inflate export data if you want to," said a customs official in China's eastern Zhejiang province, an export powerhouse.
Chinese customs headquarters didn't respond to requests to comment. In the past, they have defended the data. "The customs data is based on invoices submitted by companies," the General Administration of Customs said in January. "Every dollar in the data corresponds to a real invoice," it said.
Hong Kong's Customs & Excise Department and Census & Statistics Department said failure to lodge an accurate export-import declaration could result in prosecution.
The exact reasons for the widening discrepancy aren't clear. Economists said the need to evade China's system of capital controls, which make it difficult to move investment funds in and out of the country, could be a powerful motivator. By labeling goods as valued higher than their real worth and sending them abroad, a person or company can bring in extra money from outside the mainland.
In the past few months, investors have had added motivation for evading controls. Mainland equity markets ended a weak 2012 with a strong rise, property prices began rising again and the yuan gained against the dollar.
Over-invoicing exports to bring funds into the country is common practice, said the chief executive of a U.S. sporting-goods company with factories in Guangdong -- adding that it isn't a practice the company follows.
-- Yajun Zhang, Richard Silk and Tom Orlik

Corporate News: Global Airline-Passenger Traffic Continues to Rebound

Author: Cameron, Doug

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 04 Apr 2013: B.9.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/corporate-news-global-airline-passenger-traffic/docview/1323193721/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: The growth in flying has almost doubled over the past five months from the sluggish rates seen in the first half of last year, though cargo traffic remains slack, and some big domestic markets -- including India and Brazil -- continue to shrink, the International Air Transport Association said.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Corporate+News%3A+Global+Airline-Passenger+Traffic+Continues+to+Rebound&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-04&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=B.9&amp;au=Cameron%2C+Doug&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Global airline-passenger traffic remains on track for double-digit growth this year as a rebounding Chinese market leads broader expansion by carriers in Asia and the Middle East, according to industry data published Wednesday.
The growth in flying has almost doubled over the past five months from the sluggish rates seen in the first half of last year, though cargo traffic remains slack, and some big domestic markets -- including India and Brazil -- continue to shrink, the International Air Transport Association said.
The airline business is viewed as a leading indicator of broader economic growth, and the Geneva-based trade group said global passenger traffic in February rose 3.7% from a year earlier and was up 1.2% from January.
The gain outstripped the rise in airline capacity, pushing the average load factor -- the percentage of seats filled -- to a record high.
China's domestic market has driven the broader recovery, with traffic surging 20% in February, or 13% after stripping out the effect of the Lunar New Year, a prime time for leisure travel. Last year, the holiday fell in January.
Other big domestic markets continued to shrink, with U.S. carriers cutting capacity to boost their pricing power while cautioning that automatic government budget cuts are starting to hurt business.
US Airways Group Inc. on Wednesday reiterated a warning given by larger rival Delta Air Lines Inc. that the so-called sequester spending cuts in the U.S. government budget are hurting late bookings, which usually command higher fares.
U.S. carriers have led the global industry in trimming capacity to match demand, andAnalyst Daniel McKenzie at Buckingham Research Group on Wednesday flagged further cuts planned for the Northern Hemisphere's coming summer season, traditionally the industry's peak period for travel and earnings. "Capacity has come out of the industry and is mostly staying out," Mr. McKenzie said in a note to clients.
China's big airlines are leveraging their more robust home market to increase international growth. In the second quarter, Air China Ltd. is boosting the number of seats offered on flights to the U.S. by 55%, compared with a year earlier, while China Southern Airlines Co. is adding 73% more capacity, according to Buckingham.
Buckingham's analysis shows U.S. and European airlines returning to modest growth in the second quarter after shrinking in the first three months of the year, while big Middle East and Asian carriers plan more rapid expansion.
India's domestic traffic fell 9.1%.

World News: China Conflicted on Its Stance Toward the North

Author: Page, Jeremy

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 02 Apr 2013: A.9.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-china-conflicted-on-stance-toward/docview/1322194127/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: [...]China is unlikely to adopt major changes to its North Korea policy, analysts and diplomats say.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+China+Conflicted+on+Its+Stance+Toward+the+North&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-04-02&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.9&amp;au=Page%2C+Jeremy&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   BEIJING -- The unusually robust U.S. measures to North Korea's latest threats have complicated the response of China's new leadership to Pyongyang.
Many observers see evidence that the leadership is increasingly frustrated by the failure of its North Korea policy, and concerned about the prospects of another military clash on its border. But those concerns are still outweighed by military commanders' desire to maintain Pyongyang as a strategic buffer against the U.S. -- a desire that has intensified as a result of the U.S. "pivot" toward Asia.
When Deng Yuwen, an editor at a prominent Communist Party newspaper, wrote an op-ed article titled "China should abandon North Korea" in February, it was hailed by many diplomats as a sign that Beijing was reviewing ties with its neighbor following the most recent nuclear test there.
But soon after the opinion column was published in the Financial Times, Mr. Deng was punished with a monthlong suspension from his job at the Study Times, according to people familiar with the matter.
On Monday, when contacted, Mr. Deng told The Wall Street Journal, "I can't accept interviews about this. Please understand the situation."
Mr. Deng's punishment highlights the conflicted response of China's new leadership to North Korea's repeated threats.
While several academics have called for China to downgrade ties, or reduce aid and investment, Mr. Deng went a step further in the February editorial and urged Beijing to pursue Korean reunification.
Beijing sees the recent U.S. moves to strengthen its missile-defense system and fly advanced bombers and fighter jets to South Korea as direct threats to its security interests. But it sees a greater threat in the prospect of North Korea collapsing or reunifying with the South, both of which it believes would help the U.S. to "contain" China.
China -- still by far the North's biggest aid donor, investor and trade partner -- has also long worried a regime collapse there would trigger a flood of refugees into northeastern China.
As a result, China is unlikely to adopt major changes to its North Korea policy, analysts and diplomats say.
Beijing has indicated its displeasure with North Korea's latest nuclear test by backing new U.N. sanctions against Pyongyang and slowing some cross-border trade with tighter customs inspections, the diplomats and analysts say.
Chinese customs figures show that exports of rice to North Korea dropped to zero in January, before rebounding in February, and crude-oil exports to the country also dropped to zero in February. With official data on crude-oil exports in March not yet available, it remains unclear whether those declines were cyclical, or the result of a policy decision in Beijing.
But even if those were punitive measures, many analysts say Beijing has taken such steps before with negligible effects on Pyongyang's leadership. They also say China is unlikely to go further this time given recent U.S. moves to bolster defense ties in Asia.
"North Korea ultimately knows that if it dies, China becomes more insecure," said Shen Dingli, vice dean of the Institute of International Affairs at Fudan University in Shanghai.
"At the end of the day, the DPRK [North Korea] is not China's enemy," said Mr. Shen, using the North's formal name, the Democratic People's Republic of Korea.
Mr. Shen is one of the academics who have argued publicly in favor of downgrading China's relationship with North Korea. He and other Chinese international-relations experts say there is an unusually open debate going on in policy-making circles about how to redefine China's ties with North Korea.
But academics like Mr. Shen may have limited influence on party leaders, especially relative to the People's Liberation Army, which is preoccupied with ways to counteract U.S. military influence in Asia, according to several experts and diplomats.
Commentators linked to the Chinese military have taken a different tack, arguing that China should strengthen its relations with North Korea to counterbalance U.S. efforts to contain China through the strategic "pivot."
A recent commentary in the People's Liberation Army Daily blamed the U.S. for the instability on the Korean peninsula: "The main reason why North Korea is bent on developing nuclear weapons is basically the threat that the U.S. poses to its security."
General Zhu Chenghu of China's National Defense University made a similar argument in a presentation at the University of Denver's Jackson/Ho China Forum in February, according to a video available online.
He blamed successive U.S. administrations for provoking North Korea into pursuing nuclear weapons. "They [the North Koreans] are poor," he said. "Maybe in their understanding, development of nuclear weapons is the best way to protect their national security."

Full text:   BEIJING -- More than a quarter of U.S. businesses in China said in a new survey that proprietary data was stolen from their China operations, highlighting a growing trade irritant between Washington and Beijing.
The survey of U.S. business executives released Friday by the American Chamber of Commerce in China showed that 26% had seen data or trade secrets stolen over an unspecified time period. More than 40% said they saw the risk of a data breach in their China operations rising. The chamber hasn't released surveys over data theft before.
The survey also showed U.S. businesses are increasingly worried about China's rising labor costs, slowing economic growth and the sluggish pace of economic reform, even as most said they remain optimistic about the near-term business outlook for the world's No. 2 economy.
The survey was taken late last year, before the U.S. began pressing China over accusations that state-sponsored groups were behind a series of hacking attempts on U.S. companies.
Christian Murck, the chamber's president, told reporters on Friday that data theft was "beginning to become public in a way that it hasn't in the past."
This month, U.S. National Security Adviser Thomas Donilon called on the Chinese government to stop what the Obama administration has said is a large number of hacking attacks against U.S. companies. China has repeatedly said it doesn't sponsor hacking and says China is often itself the victim of hacking attacks.

Landing a North Korean Coin Flip

Author: Gronholt-Pedersen, Jacob

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 29 Mar 2013: C.1.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/landing-north-korean-coin-flip/docview/1321314110/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: According to North Korea's state-controlled news agency, gold coins were last minted in 2012 to commemorate Kim Jong Il, the country's leader who died in late-2011.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Landing+a+North+Korean+Coin+Flip&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-29&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=C.1&amp;au=Gronholt-Pedersen%2C+Jacob&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   SINGAPORE -- Amid heightened tensions on the Korean peninsula, investor Jim Rogers is choosing sides -- financially, anyway: He is going long on rare North Korean coins.
But his reasons aren't likely to please Kim Jong Eun.
This weekend, at the Singapore International Coin Fair, a North Korean company will give collectors an unusual opportunity to buy the country's gold or silver minted coins.
It is unclear what Pyongyang-based Korea Pugang Coins Corp. will be peddling, though it sold gold coins last year. The company couldn't be reached for comment.
"They are very discreet and don't disclose much information," said a spokeswoman for the fair, who confirmed that the company booked a stand for the weekend, its second visit to the event.
According to North Korea's state-controlled news agency, gold coins were last minted in 2012 to commemorate Kim Jong Il, the country's leader who died in late-2011. The inscription: "The Great Leader Comrade Kim Jong Il Will Always Be Alive."
Mr. Kim was succeeded by his son, Kim Jong Eun.
Whatever it is selling, Korea Pugang can be confident it will find a buyer in Mr. Rogers, an American commodities investor now based in Singapore.
Mr. Rogers, 70 years old, who started the Quantum Fund with George Soros in the 1970s, bought up the entire lot of North Korean gold coins offered last year.
"If the North Koreans come again, I will do the same," Mr. Rogers said. "Coins and stamps are the only way I can invest in North Korea."
By invest in, Mr. Rogers means he wants to wager against the long-term prospects for the isolated, economically struggling country. He views his purchase as a bet on the collapse of North Korea.
"At some point down the line, North Korea will cease existing as a country. Then the value of the coins will go up," Mr. Rogers said. He wouldn't say how many coins he bought last year or what he paid.
Mr. Rogers is a fervent believer that the commodities bull-run will continue and that China and other Asian nations will set the global economic agenda for this century. He advocates investing in frontier markets such as Myanmar and Cambodia, and in 2007, sold his New York mansion and moved to Singapore, in part because he thinks it is crucial for his children to learn Mandarin.
The coin fair follows a week in which North Korea cut the military hotline to its southern neighbor and put its rocket and artillery units on "highest alert." The threat came after the U.S. and South Korea signed a military contingency plan to respond to possible attacks from North Korea.
Trade sanctions prevent citizens of the U.S. and other countries from trading precious metals with North Korean government bodies, but the coin fair spokeswoman said Korea Pugang is a private company.
Although North Korea has minted gold coins regularly since 1987, the coins are rarely sold to international investors.
The coin fair is one of the most important in Asia and draws buyers from all over the world.
"I will take a look at the coins" on Friday, said William Ng, a coin collector for 30 years and owner of the William Ng Collections shop in Singapore. "I'm not sure I'd be able to sell them here in Singapore," he said, adding that he has never had any requests for North Korean coins.
Estonia-based Tavex Group, a firm that specializes in gold and currencies, made a deal with Pyongyang in 2008 to sell North Korean gold coins.
But the North Koreans ended it after the first shipment of coins from a 2007 series featuring elephants, rhinos, owls, lions and buffalos.
"We sold them at a relatively high price to collectors, but demand was not big," says Tomas Pavelson, who works in sales at Tavex Group.
"Actually, we still have one left."
Representatives of six gold dealers participating in this weekend's fair in Singapore said they had never bought or sold or even had any requests for North Korean coins.
At Oklahoma City-based Apmex, the largest online precious metals dealer in terms of sales in the U.S., no North Korean coins were on sale.
But on eBay, two North Korean one-ounce gold coins were on offer Thursday, from 1988 and 2002, at $2,790 each.
That is well above Thursday's closing gold price of $1594.80 an ounce.
