China Worries Arise in Sprint Deal

Author: Ante, Spencer E; Yadron, Danny; Gryta, Thomas

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 28 Mar 2013: A.1.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/china-worries-arise-sprint-deal/docview/1320098896/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: Negotiations are continuing on the U.S.'s conditions for blessing the Sprint deal, but the government is expected to require the companies to notify it when they plan to buy equipment for the core of their network and to cooperate if any national-security or public-safety considerations arise, the people familiar with the matter said. Because of concerns about violating trade rules, any constraints wouldn't specifically exclude gear from Huawei, which Softbank has used in its home market of Japan, or ZTE, a person familiar with the process said.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=China+Worries+Arise+in+Sprint+Deal&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-28&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.1&amp;au=Ante%2C+Spencer+E%3BYadron%2C+Danny%3BGryta%2C+Thomas&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   The U.S. government is seeking oversight of network-equipment purchases as a condition for approving Softbank Corp.'s $20 billion acquisition of U.S. phone carrier Sprint Nextel Corp., a move that appears to be aimed at keeping out Chinese suppliers like Huawei Technologies Co., people familiar with the matter said.
U.S. treatment of those suppliers has inflamed tensions between the U.S. and China, which are already sparring over accusations of computer hacking and trade issues. After the House intelligence committee concluded in October that Huawei and Chinese rival ZTE Corp. pose national-security risks because their equipment could be used for spying, China's Commerce Ministry lashed out, saying the report violated the U.S.'s free-market principles and warning it could undermine cooperation between the countries.
Negotiations are continuing on the U.S.'s conditions for blessing the Sprint deal, but the government is expected to require the companies to notify it when they plan to buy equipment for the core of their network and to cooperate if any national-security or public-safety considerations arise, the people familiar with the matter said.
Because of concerns about violating trade rules, any constraints wouldn't specifically exclude gear from Huawei, which Softbank has used in its home market of Japan, or ZTE, a person familiar with the process said. Nor would they explicitly give the government a veto, this person said. But U.S. officials have made no secret of their distrust of the Chinese companies and are aiming to make sure their equipment doesn't become a core part of U.S. telecom infrastructure, the people said.
"You have to find a way to say, 'Don't buy from the Chinese,' without saying, 'Don't buy from the Chinese,'" said a person who has spoken with Sprint.
Sprint and Softbank both declined to comment Wednesday. In interviews when their deal was announced in October, chief executives at both companies acknowledged U.S. concerns about Chinese suppliers.
Both companies are willing to forgo use of Huawei and ZTE gear in the core of their U.S. network, said the person who has spoken with Sprint.
Huawei and ZTE have denied they would let the Chinese government use their gear for surveillance. Huawei spokesman William Plummer said all vendors rely on global supply chains, and the company's products are used in nearly 150 markets, including almost every country in Europe.
"The adoption of such a policy would seem little more than a market-distorting political or protectionist exercise," Mr. Plummer said, referring to a review of equipment purchases that could exclude Huawei.
"It's a pity that U.S. carriers cannot use our equipment," said ZTE spokesman David Dai Shu. "We are trying to prove that ZTE's equipment is safe and poses no threat to U.S. security."
U.S. carriers are concerned that their options are shrinking as the Western telecom-equipment industry struggles. Huawei is the world's second-largest telecom-equipment provider behind Sweden's Ericsson, and ZTE is the sixth, according to technology-research firm IDC.
Much of the rest of the industry is under stress, with Alcatel-Lucent SA of France burning through cash and Nokia Siemens Networks having cut nearly a quarter of its workforce to stay competitive. Nokia Siemens Networks is a joint venture of Finland's Nokia Corp. and Germany's Siemens AG.
Huawei, which grew quickly by being a low-cost supplier, is now outspending most of its rivals on research and development, making it increasingly competitive on the technology front. While smaller U.S. operators use the Chinese company's equipment, the U.S. government has waved off major U.S. carriers.
In 2010, then-Commerce Secretary Gary Locke warned Sprint away from awarding Huawei part of a contract worth billions of dollars. Mr. Locke called Sprint CEO Dan Hesse to remind him of the U.S. government's security concerns, people familiar with the matter said at the time.
Now, U.S. officials are using this latest round of consolidation in the telecom industry to formalize their oversight of such deals.
The negotiations between Sprint, Softbank and the government are part of the national-security review required when a foreign company tries to buy control of a U.S. company.
Deutsche Telekom AG's T-Mobile USA unit and MetroPCS Communications Inc. went through the process when seeking approval for their merger. When the Federal Communications Commission approved that deal in March, the companies agreed to give the departments of Justice and Homeland Security 30 days notice before using a new vendor for network equipment. They also agreed to work out any national-security concerns the departments raise.
An FCC official said the language was requested by the departments of Justice and Homeland Security. The two departments declined to comment.
The FCC reviews all deals involving wireless carriers. But in cases involving a foreign buyer, the review is widened to a group including representatives of the departments of Justice, Defense and Homeland Security and the Federal Bureau of Investigation.
Such deals also must be cleared by the Committee on Foreign Investment in the U.S., or Cfius, a secretive panel headed up by the Treasury. Analysts expect the government to approve Softbank's deal to take control of Sprint.
"We would be compliant with the policy of the U.S. government," Softbank CEO Masayoshi Son said in an October interview when asked about using Huawei gear. He added that more than 90% of the company's total capital spending involves suppliers other than Huawei and ZTE.
A Treasury spokeswoman declined to comment, citing the confidentiality around Cfius cases.
The merged company also will likely have to create a subsidiary that handles Sprint's classified work for the government and agree to allow inspections of company facilities, isolate foreigners from certain sensitive parts of the network and require certain employee screenings, said people familiar with Cfius reviews.
The growing sensitivity toward Chinese equipment was evident in a little-noticed addition to a government-funding law signed Tuesday, in which Congress effectively banned federal dollars from being spent on information technology from companies "owned, directed or subsidized by the People's Republic of China."
One issue for Sprint and Softbank is that Clearwire Corp., a wireless company that Sprint is in the process of acquiring, uses some Huawei radio base stations to transmit phone calls and data.
Clearwire Chief Technology Officer John Saw said Huawei accounts for a small part of Clearwire's infrastructure, the company is reducing its use of Huawei gear and that every LTE base station will be tested to for security weaknesses. "It is important to point out that there are no longer any domestic suppliers for radio base station infrastructure equipment," he said. "Clearwire is committed to ensuring that our network and our customers' data are secure."

World News: Brics Nations Take Steps on Currency Trade, Bank

Author: McGroarty, Patrick; Maylie, Devon

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 27 Mar 2013: A.8.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-brics-nations-take-steps-on-currency/docview/1319620313/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: [...]we agreed that we will continue to work on creating a Brics bank once the unresolved questions are answered," the Interfax news agency quoted Mr. Siluanov as saying.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+Brics+Nations+Take+Steps+on+Currency+Trade%2C+Bank&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-27&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.8&amp;au=McGroarty%2C+Patrick%3BMaylie%2C+Devon&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Members of the Brics group of emerging markets took steps to trade their currencies more freely and to establish a joint development bank, seeking to counter the influence that developed countries exert over the global economy.
Brazil and China agreed Tuesday at a summit of Brics leaders in Durban, South Africa, to use their central banks to swap up to $30 billion in Brazilian real and Chinese yuan over the next three years, allowing businesses to trade between the two countries without converting earnings and investments to U.S. dollars, the standard conduit of global trade.
Brazil's finance minister, Guido Mantega, said the arrangement, which the countries have been working toward since this past June, would give them a means to exchange currencies "independent of the conditions of financial markets." He also said the Brics countries -- Brazil, Russia, India, China and South Africa -- were close to an agreement to pool some foreign-currency reserves in case of a balance-of-payments crisis.
The bloc's move to create a new development bank, however, was weighed down by disagreements over funding and management, said Russian Finance Minister Anton Siluanov. "On the whole, we agreed that we will continue to work on creating a Brics bank once the unresolved questions are answered," the Interfax news agency quoted Mr. Siluanov as saying.
South Africa's finance minister, Pravin Gordhan, added that he was pleased with the negotiations. "We're on track," he said.
South African officials want a new development bank to fund infrastructure projects that the International Monetary Fund and the World Bank have overlooked. Larger Brics members, such as China and India, are eager to establish an institution that could extend their influence deeper into Africa and other emerging markets where their economic interests are expanding.
The Brics' slow march toward establishing their own bank illustrates their struggle to move past populist rhetoric to true cooperation between powerful and sometimes adversarial nations. Each is eager to reap the benefits of a larger trade group -- and all are fearful of being flooded with products from the others, particularly China.
"What we now seek to address jointly is to find the means towards a more equitable balance of trade," South Africa's President Jacob Zuma told reporters in South Africa's capital, Pretoria, after meeting with China's President Xi Jinping. "Africa is counting on the People's Republic of China for support in the continent's development."
Mr. Xi acknowledged China is pursuing its own commercial interests in Africa. "We each see the other side as an opportunity for our own development," he said.
According to the proposals discussed Tuesday, each country would likely contribute up to $10 billion to the bank, an official said, speaking before plans were to be approved by the national leaders gathering Wednesday. The bank would focus on infrastructure development, he said, both in the five-nation group and in emerging markets where they want to do business.
But economists and business leaders said an initial pool of $50 billion wouldn't be enough for the bank to make its mark in Africa or elsewhere.
"At this point it's somewhat symbolic," said Anthony Thunstrom, chief operating officer for accounting firm KPMG LLP's Africa investment program. "Its potential will only be realized when it's better capitalized, and I think that's going to be a longer-term project."
More specific decisions -- including which country will host the bank and where it will invest -- will be postponed at least until the bloc's next summit meeting in Brazil in 2014, he said.
"There is general agreement that there is a need for this," said the official involved in the negotiations. "Creating a multilateral institution takes quite a long time from being an idea to being set up."
---
Gregory L. White contributed to this article.
Subscribe to WSJ:
Credit: Patrick McGroarty; Devon Maylie

Subject: Currency; Foreign exchange; Global economy; Development banks; Emerging markets

Business indexing term: Subject: Currency Foreign exchange Global economy Development banks Emerging markets

World News: Japan, EU To Start Trade Talks

Author: Obe, Mitsuru; Sekiguchi, Toko

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 26 Mar 2013: A.7.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-japan-eu-start-trade-talks/docview/1319366091/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: Japan and the European Union agreed to start negotiations on a free-trade agreement, after a decision by Tokyo to join talks for a U.S.-led pan-Pacific free-trade pact.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+Japan%2C+EU+To+Start+Trade+Talks&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-26&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.7&amp;au=Obe%2C+Mitsuru%3BSekiguchi%2C+Toko&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   TOKYO -- Japan and the European Union agreed to start negotiations on a free-trade agreement, after a decision by Tokyo to join talks for a U.S.-led pan-Pacific free-trade pact.
The announcement came as Japan and the EU try to spur their economies, which are struggling with fiscal crises and aging populations.
Japanese officials said they are looking beyond economic weaknesses in Europe and trying to strengthen partnerships with Europe's advanced economies to speed Japan's structural reforms.
Japanese trade officials said they hope to wrap up the talks in about two years. Japan is set to start trade talks with China and South Korea this week.
The rapid succession of trade talks partly represents an effort by Japan to catch up with South Korea, an economic rival that already has trade deals with the EU and the U.S. and is rapidly eclipsing Japan in areas such as electronics.
On Japan's wish list in European talks are the elimination of the EU's 14% tariffs on electronics and 10% tariffs on autos, both of which have put Japanese exporters at a disadvantage to their Korean rivals.
Japan also hopes a trade deal will attract more European companies to Japan and stimulate the domestic economy.
Europe has strength in areas where Japan faces severe challenges, such as electric-power supply, following the 2011 nuclear accident at the Fukushima Daiichi nuclear plant.
The talks had been expected to start in 2011; the delay is an indication of how contentious such trade pacts are in both Japan and EU.
The EU demand that Japan open its wine and cheese markets looks certain to invite opposition from Japanese farmers. Meanwhile, Germany is cautious that a free-trade agreement would mean a flood of Japanese cars into its market. The EU is Japan's fourth-largest export market after China, the Association of Southeast Asian Nations, and the U.S., with a share of over 10%.

World News: South Korea, Tokyo Seek Thaw, Nudged by U.S. --- By Yuka Hayashi in Tokyo and Alastair Gale in Seoul

Author: Hayashi, Yuka; Gale, Alastair

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 26 Mar 2013: A.7.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-south-korea-tokyo-seek-thaw-nudged-u-s/docview/1319364546/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: In mid-January, shortly after Mr. Abe again suggested his government might rescind Tokyo's apology for the use of Korean sex slaves by its military in the early 20th century, Kurt Campbell, assistant secretary of state for East Asia at that time, flew to Tokyo with two other top Obama administration officials.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+South+Korea%2C+Tokyo+Seek+Thaw%2C+Nudged+by+U.S.+---+By+Yuka+Hayashi+in+Tokyo+and+Alastair+Gale+in+Seoul&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-26&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.7&amp;au=Hayashi%2C+Yuka%3BGale%2C+Alastair&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Japan and South Korea are haltingly moving to mend their bruised relationship, encouraged by U.S. officials eager to maintain a united front of allies as China's influence rises across the region and as North Korea has stepped up its bellicose rhetoric.
Signs of a thaw have come as both countries have installed new leaders and as Washington has expressed growing impatience with repeated flare-ups over disagreements left unresolved since World War II.
Efforts to rebuild trust between Seoul and Tokyo -- which all but suspended top-level diplomatic dialogues last summer amid territorial tensions -- have been under way since January, soon after both countries' elections.
Eager not to let deep-seated bitterness over Japan's wartime record in Korea derail security strategies in Asia, U.S. officials have played a prominent role in encouraging better relations between the governments of South Korean President Park Geun-hye and Japanese Prime Minister Shinzo Abe.
When Ms. Park was inaugurated in February, Japan's deputy prime minister attended as well as 30 members of parliament and three former prime ministers. A week later, Ms. Park and Mr. Abe talked, pledging to work together to implement United Nations sanctions against North Korea in response to its Feb. 12 nuclear test.
Momentum toward normalcy could build over the coming months. Senior officials from the two nations and China are set to kick off talks in Seoul on Tuesday for a trilateral free-trade agreement, an initiative that has endured tensions among all three nations. Leaders from the three are also expected to meet in South Korea in May.
"Japan and Korea are precious neighbors that share basic values and interests. We want to communicate frequently," Japanese Foreign Minister Fumio Kishida told reporters after talking to Yun Byung-se, his counterpart, on the phone last week.
Mr. Yun described Japan as "an important neighbor to work with for peace and cooperation in Northeast Asia." He said the two countries should take the opportunity of their new governments to enhance trust.
Such comments represent a change from fiery rhetoric late last summer, when former South Korean President Lee Myung-bak visited Korean-controlled islets that are also claimed by Japan and called them "worthy of sacrificing our lives."
Japan's then-prime minister criticized Seoul for "illegally" occupying the islands and Japan's parliament denounced the South Korean trip.
The inauguration of Ms. Park took Mr. Lee out of the equation and gave Tokyo a chance to approach the Korean side.
Added to that was pressure from Washington. Troubled by Japan's entanglements with both Beijing and Seoul, and alarmed by hawkish policies advertised by Mr. Abe and his party during their election campaign last year, U.S. officials repeatedly urged Tokyo to make efforts to normalize ties with Seoul.
In mid-January, shortly after Mr. Abe again suggested his government might rescind Tokyo's apology for the use of Korean sex slaves by its military in the early 20th century, Kurt Campbell, assistant secretary of state for East Asia at that time, flew to Tokyo with two other top Obama administration officials. The Americans warned Japanese officials not to bring up sensitive issues related to Japan's past with Koreans, saying it would further complicate the country's relationship with Seoul, people familiar with the meetings said.
Mr. Abe has generally kept mum on historical issues since taking office, while focusing on how to stimulate Japan's economy. In other steps, a senior lawmaker visited Seoul in early January, followed by a visit by a larger group of politicians.
But behind the signs of a thaw, serious animosities persist. Conversations between top officials have included remarks underlining a gaping divide in views over Japan's wartime activities. "The governments in both Tokyo and Seoul. . . know well that any concessions would risk them politically at home," said Yang Moo-jin, a professor at the University of North Korean Studies in Seoul.
In Tokyo, opposition lawmaker Seiji Maehara, a former foreign minister, was similarly pessimistic. "I don't think we have a situation where Japan and Korea, and Japan and China, can talk to each other with trust," he said.
The potential for historical issues to derail security ties between South Korea and Japan was made clear last year when an agreement for the limited sharing of intelligence information by the countries' militaries was scrapped at the 11th hour because of objections raised by politicians in South Korea.

China Puts More FX Meat on Chopping Block

Author: Orlik, Tom

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 26 Mar 2013: C.8.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/china-puts-more-fx-meat-on-chopping-block/docview/1319364516/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: [Financial Analysis and Commentary] A member of China's monetary-policy committee says the country's foreign-exchange reserves are like a slab of meat on the block in the U.S. Those choice words reflect fear that U.S. quantitative easing will lead to a falling dollar and higher inflation, chopping the value of China's $3.3 trillion stash.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=China+Puts+More+FX+Meat+on+Chopping+Block&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-26&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=C.8&amp;au=Orlik%2C+Tom&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   [Financial Analysis and Commentary]
A member of China's monetary-policy committee says the country's foreign-exchange reserves are like a slab of meat on the block in the U.S.
Those choice words reflect fear that U.S. quantitative easing will lead to a falling dollar and higher inflation, chopping the value of China's $3.3 trillion stash.
That doesn't seem to have stopped China from making a record addition to its dollar reserves in January. Data from the U.S. Treasury show China added $51.3 billion to its dollar holdings, mainly in the form of Treasury notes and bonds. That tops a previous record of $36.9 billion in May 2008, when global imbalances were at their precrisis peak.
It also is a reversal of the trend in the past two years, when China's accumulation of reserves and dollar purchases slowed markedly. China added just $130.4 billion to its FX reserves in 2012, down from $461.9 billion in 2007.
The dollar share of reserves -- which are also allocated to euros, yen and other currencies -- appears to have fallen to about 49% from about 69% over the same period.
Record purchases of Treasurys in January suggest imbalances in trade and capital flows are back in play. China's trade surplus has returned to levels last seen in 2008. Capital, flowing out of the country for much of 2012, now appears to be flowing in, with the latest round of quantitative easing in the U.S. a contributing factor.
January's data overstate the scale of the reversal. Chinese firms were trying to unload dollars throughout the fourth quarter of 2012, but with the central bank staying out of the markets, there was no one there to buy.
The central bank seems to have waded back in at the end of the year -- perhaps to head off pressure for yuan appreciation, and suddenly accumulated several months of dollar inflows to invest.
The conclusion remains the same. Trade and capital inflows that fuel yuan-appreciation pressure have eased compared with the precrisis years, but they haven't disappeared. China's government complains about dollar depreciation and U.S. inflation cutting the meat from their FX reserves. But if Beijing wants to stop the yuan from rising, it will have to continue putting more on the chopping block.

China Flips Switch to Fancy Exports

Author: Frangos, Alex

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 25 Mar 2013: B.1.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/china-flips-switch-fancy-exports/docview/1319189790/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: China has been increasing exports in industries as varied as computers, car parts, high-technology lamps and optical-surgical equipment, according to a Wall Street Journal analysis of Chinese, European Union and U.S. trade data. [...]China's exports contain a rising percentage of materials that were made in the country, according to the World Trade Organization and the Organization for Economic Cooperation and Development.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=China+Flips+Switch+to+Fancy+Exports&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-25&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=B.1&amp;au=Frangos%2C+Alex&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   As rising labor costs push manufacturing of T-shirts, jeans and the like out of China, the country has been able to offset that loss by grabbing the high end.
And nowhere is that on better display than the San Francisco-Oakland Bay Bridge.
When the switch is flipped each night for the span's two-year artistic light show, the electricity flows through sophisticated power devices made by Gary Hua's factory not far from Shanghai.
In the six years since it was founded, his company has grown to 1,000 employees, who last year made three million power-supply units for high-efficiency light-emitting diodes. The company, Inventronics Inc., expects to double production this year and export more than half that output.
Inventronics exemplifies China's shift toward producing the higher-end products that are fueling the country's export growth. China has been increasing exports in industries as varied as computers, car parts, high-technology lamps and optical-surgical equipment, according to a Wall Street Journal analysis of Chinese, European Union and U.S. trade data.
HSBC economists estimate that China's share of global exports increased to 11% last year, from 9% before the 2008 financial crisis and around 5% at the turn of the millennium.
Chinese employment in higher-value industries such as electrical- and communications-equipment production has jumped since 2008 and now exceeds employment in textiles, garments and leather making, says Royal Bank of Scotland economist Louis Kuijs.
High-tech goods are more valuable and are a bigger market than clothes. Over the past two years, Chinese exports to the U.S. of high-tech electronics, auto parts and optical devices rose 24%, to $129 billion, while exports of clothes and footwear rose just 5% to $47 billion.
A chunk of what is marked "Made in China" is made up of parts and design that originated elsewhere, making trade data a little fuzzy. The chips in Inventronics' LED drivers are from the U.S., for example.
But China's exports contain a rising percentage of materials that were made in the country, according to the World Trade Organization and the Organization for Economic Cooperation and Development.
Mr. Hua, 48 years old, was educated in the U.S. and spent a decade there, starting an electrical-parts company. He returned to China in 1999 and came out of an early retirement in 2007 to create Inventronics.
He based the company in Hangzhou, about 110 miles from Shanghai, to tap a base of highly trained engineers and put the company's factory near its suppliers. That helps Inventronics develop new products rapidly and adapt them to customers' often narrow specifications.
"That's one of the key advantages of being located in China," Mr. Gua says.
A skilled labor force, a large domestic market and networks of suppliers have become important factors that rising wages or a stronger currency, which makes exports less cost-competitive overseas, won't snuff out quickly. And China's growing consumer market means that if higher costs make exports less profitable, manufacturers can sell more products at home.
China also benefits by comparison from rising labor and material costs in Southeast Asia and Latin America, says Mr. Kuijs, of RBS.
Talaris, which makes cash-sorting machines used by banks, last year moved production from Sweden to China, where the company employs 1,000 workers at peak production. The move has cut the cost to make each machine by more than 25% as quality has improved, the Hampshire, U.K., company says. The company's sorters and dispensers scan thousands of bills a minute while checking for counterfeits and recording serial numbers.
"You have a concentration of suppliers getting stronger and stronger and more competitive," says Talaris Chief Executive Paul Adams. Talaris considered locating its factory in Taiwan, South Korea or Southeast Asia, but China had the advantage of a web of parts suppliers that would compete with each other and keep prices low, he says.
Around 90% of the value of a Talaris cash sorter is produced within China. The sorter's high-tech sensors, which account for 10% of the cost, are made in Japan. But diodes, capacitors, steel and plastic pieces are produced in southern China's technology metropolis of Shenzhen for quick shipping 930 miles to Talaris's assembly and research-and-development facility in Shanghai.
"Labor was only a small component of decision making," Mr. Adams says. He estimates that parts account for 80% of each machine's cost, with the rest coming from labor and overhead.
Businesspeople outside China complain that Beijing gives unfair advantages to its companies through subsidies, cheap financing and by letting its currency rise more slowly than market forces would dictate.
And some people say that as China grabs a greater share of global trade, it isn't gaining ground as quickly as in the past. Earnings growth in China is slowing, indicating there will be less money to invest.
"When China exhausts its ability to waste domestic savings, people won't be as impressed by China's size," says Diana Choyleva, a China economist for Lombard Street Research.
Subscribe to WSJ:
Credit: By Alex Frangos

Subject: Exterior lighting; High technology; Manufacturing; Exports; US imports; Cost control; Automotive parts industry; Clothing; Competition

World News: South Africa Trade Hits Bump

Author: McGroarty, Patrick

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 25 Mar 2013: A.11.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/world-news-south-africa-trade-hits-bump/docview/1319187703/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: [...]imports from member countries to South Africa rose 25% annually over the past two years, while South Africa's exports to them rose just 13%.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=World+News%3A+South+Africa+Trade+Hits+Bump&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-25&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.13&amp;au=McGroarty%2C+Patrick&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   JOHANNESBURG -- South Africa joined a club called BRICS a few years ago to tighten ties with the world's largest emerging markets. Today, the embrace from outsize competitors in the club, particularly China, is suffocating South African manufacturers, executives say.
"Manufacturers need economies of scale, and we don't have that," said Stewart Jennings, chief executive of South African glassmaker PG Group Ltd. and chairman of the Manufacturing Circle, an industry group. "And I think China uses that to do what they want to do. They're the gorilla in BRICS. We're the runt."
The issue comes to light as South Africa hosts leaders from Brazil, Russia, India and China in the port city of Durban this week for a summit that aims to foster so-called South-South trade among developing economies. The bloc -- comprising Brazil, Russia, India China and South Africa -- has previously staked out positions to counterbalance American heft in the global economy.
BRICS nations have called for a global reserve currency to compete with the U.S. dollar; criticized the tight control the U.S. and Europe exercise over the World Bank and the International Monetary Fund; and said they would create their own development bank.
But the most immediate impact for South Africa has been to expose glaring weaknesses in its own economy, foreshadowing risks other African countries face as BRICS nations step up trade on the continent.
Chinese President Xi Jinping began a tour of Africa on Sunday during his first trip abroad, where he signed more than a dozen trade and cooperation deals with Tanzania.
To be sure, economists say South African manufacturers would be in even worse shape if their country hadn't joined the BRICS. The sector provides 15% of South Africa's gross domestic product and a million jobs -- more than a 10th of the workforce in a country with an official unemployment rate of 25%.
Buffeted by rising wage and utility costs unrelated to competition from BRICS countries, manufacturers have shed 85,000 jobs over the past three years.
Like other African countries, South Africa also is hobbled by a costly, undereducated workforce and neglected infrastructure that leave manufacturers vulnerable to imports from abroad. African business leaders say the continent's fragmented economies are just too small to contend with the manufacturing might of the BRICS, especially China.
"It's a serious threat to our factories," said Andries Tshabalala, executive director of Actom (Pty.) Ltd., a maker and distributor of electrical equipment. After customers switched to cheaper Chinese imports, Actom scaled back several product lines. "South Africa just can't afford to lose these jobs," he said.
South Africa was never supposed to be part of the club.
The group grew out of Goldman Sachs economist Jim O'Neill's bet that those big emerging economies were poised to challenge traditional powers like the U.S. and Germany as global leaders. The countries invited South Africa to join the annual summit beginning in 2011, largely to have a representative from Africa in the club.
South Africa hasn't kept up with its new peers. In the past three years, South Africa's rate of growth has been the bloc's slowest by a full percentage point. In recent weeks, its currency fell to four-year lows -- outpacing declines of other emerging-market currencies -- as concerns have mounted over South Africa's economic outlook and political stability.
South Africa's BRICS membership hasn't come with any market-opening obligations, but manufacturers complain the government hasn't fought very hard on their behalf, either. As a result, imports from member countries to South Africa rose 25% annually over the past two years, while South Africa's exports to them rose just 13%.
South Africa runs a trade deficit of nearly $1 billion with Brazil, for example, and last year chicken farmers complained that cheap imports from the South American country were killing their business.
When South Africa imposed steep tariffs, Brazil complained to the World Trade Organization, and Pretoria backpedaled. In December, Trade Minister Rob Davies dropped the tariffs, saying the government would instead investigate a "comprehensive strategy" that didn't target any one country.
South Africa's lone stainless-steel manufacturer says it also confronts hurdles abroad that its competitors don't face to enter South Africa. "Anybody can send their steel here with no duties, yet in a lot of these other countries we face quite significant duties of up to 25%," said Dave Martin, CEO of Columbus Stainless (Pty.) Ltd. "Our government is a lot slower to take decisions on trade issues, for fear of upsetting very large trade partners."
South African officials say they want to change the trade balance dynamic. The country's biggest trade deficit is with China, a figure that reached $4 billion last year.
"We are where we are but that's not where we want to be," Finance Minister Pravin Gordhan said in an interview last week.
He said he planned to lobby fellow BRICS nations for more balanced trade between those countries and all of Africa.

For Hess, Norway Interest?

Author: Denning, Liam

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 25 Mar 2013: C.1.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/hess-norway-interest/docview/1319186497/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: [...]in 18 of the past 20 quarters, its main exploration-and -production business has ranked no higher than fourth out of a peer group of seven in terms of return on capital employed, a key measure of whether a company is creating value, according to Doug Terreson, analyst at ISI Group. For most of the past decade, Hess's stock has traded at wide discounts to the average for the same peer group in terms of price to cash flow, an important metric for the capital-intensive oil sector. [...]if the $5.7 billion valuation Deutsche Bank puts on Hess's logistical, refining and marketing assets is stripped out, then Statoil would be paying about $21 for each barrel of oil equivalent of proved reserves.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=For+Hess%2C+Norway+Interest%3F&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-25&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=C.1&amp;au=Denning%2C+Liam&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   [Financial Analysis and Commentary]
In the fight for Hess, the son of the oil company's founder stands in one corner. Opposite is an activist hedge fund not known for taking prisoners. Other shareholders are caught in the middle.
Might a mediator come from Norway, of all places?
Elliott Management, which owns 4.4% of Hess, is pushing the company to break itself up and aims to put five directors on the 14-member board when shareholders meet in May. Hess, whose Chairman and Chief Executive John Hess effectively controls just over 10% of the company, has responded with a plan to sell assets, return cash and appoint six new directors.
Both plans carry risk. Elliott's governance reforms are welcome, but its break-up plan is complex, and several analysts have expressed doubts about the viability of the proposed mainly international business.
Hess's counterattack offers benefits in the form of accelerated streamlining of its business and some new blood on the board. Still, investors would have to maintain faith that Hess could deliver despite a weak governance record and years of lagging shareholder returns.
But there is an alternative: selling Hess outright.
A standard reason for selling is the realization a company's assets might be worth more if run by someone else -- something activist campaigns can crystallize. Hess has some desirable assets, particularly in the Bakken shale formation, Gulf of Mexico, North Sea and Asia's Malay Basin.
But, recent success in Ghana aside, its exploration record has been poor. And in 18 of the past 20 quarters, its main exploration-and -production business has ranked no higher than fourth out of a peer group of seven in terms of return on capital employed, a key measure of whether a company is creating value, according to Doug Terreson, analyst at ISI Group. Those peers include Apache and Devon Energy.
The result: For most of the past decade, Hess's stock has traded at wide discounts to the average for the same peer group in terms of price to cash flow, an important metric for the capital-intensive oil sector.
Despite its valuation gap, no one has stepped up to buy Hess, most likely because it wasn't perceived as being for sale.
But a bidder could emerge if shareholder sentiment was seen to be turning against the current board in the run-up to May's meeting.
Granted, broken up, Hess's separate pieces would make easier mouthfuls for a range of companies.
For the U.S. assets, these could include western majors and E&P companies, such as Continental Resources. For the rest, national oil companies from China and elsewhere might be interested.
While this ultimately could yield a higher total price, it also is riskier given the complex sale process.
A sale of the whole company would be preferable, even if Hess's scale and U.S. identity would limit the pool of potential buyers.
Assuming a 30% takeover premium, Hess would carry a price tag, including assumed net debt, of about $39 billion.
That would equate to a share price of about $91. On Friday, the shares closed at $70.27.
Western majors, including the usual suspects of Chevron and possibly Exxon Mobil, could be natural buyers for the whole company. But one other intriguing possibility is Norway's Statoil, which is 67% state-owned.
Hess's portfolio would tick several boxes for Statoil.
The Norwegian giant made a splash in 2011 when it agreed to buy Brigham Exploration for $4.4 billion. The acquisition gave Statoil positions it operated itself, as opposed to passive stakes, in the Bakken shale.
Buying Hess would augment this and further Statoil's strategy of reducing its dependence on its home country, which in 2012 accounted for two-thirds of its output.
Oswald Clint, an analyst at Sanford C. Bernstein, believes Statoil, along with BP, is one of the more-likely candidates among European oil majors to consider acquisitions.
That is due in part to its high exposure to offshore fields that tend to see steep declines in output over time. This puts an onus on securing long-lived reserves, such as shale assets.
Indeed, at just 7.4 years, Statoil has among the lowest proved-reserves life of the major oil companies.
Owning Hess would boost that to almost eight years. Other Hess assets, notably its stake in Norway's Valhall field and its operated projects in the Gulf of Mexico, also would fit well. Statoil declined to comment.
And if the $5.7 billion valuation Deutsche Bank puts on Hess's logistical, refining and marketing assets is stripped out, then Statoil would be paying about $21 for each barrel of oil equivalent of proved reserves.
That is less than Statoil spends to find and develop reserves itself.
At just under half Statoil's own enterprise value, including net debt, of $88 billion, buying Hess at a 30% premium would be a stretch, but manageable. Statoil's net debt to estimated 2013 earnings before interest, tax, depreciation and amortization would rise but still be less than one times, before factoring in any cost savings or likely asset disposals.
Assuming a cost of debt of around 5.5% -- higher than where Statoil's current debt trades -- the deal also would boost Statoil's earnings per share in 2013 by about 9%, based on current estimates for both companies.
For Hess's shareholders, a takeover price of about $91 a share would still be below the bottom end of Elliott's theoretical, and optimistic, break-up valuation of about $97 to $126.
But it would be the highest price Hess's stock has commanded since September 2008 and also substantially higher than the $49 to $55 range where Elliott likely bought most of its stake.
And if it avoided a protracted battle, as well as the risks around the current two opposing plans, shareholders should welcome a bid.

Corporate News: Tiffany Projects a Rough Start but a Brighter Finish for Its Year

Author: Warner, Melodie; Talley, Karen

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 25 Mar 2013: B.6.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/corporate-news-tiffany-projects-rough-start/docview/1319173709/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: Tiffany has plans for an Art Deco collection of silver, onyx and freshwater pearls this spring, as a less-expensive complement to 1920s-style platinum and diamond jewelry it recently created.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Corporate+News%3A+Tiffany+Projects+a+Rough+Start+but+a+Brighter+Finish+for+Its+Year&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-25&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=B.6&amp;au=Warner%2C+Melodie%3BTalley%2C+Karen&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Tiffany & Co., which posted lackluster sales for its fiscal fourth quarter, expects to muddle through a rocky start for the current year before business picks up.
The high-end jewelry retailer said earnings for its fourth quarter rose just 0.7% from prior-year results that were weighed down by costs to relocate its headquarters.
Investors appeared encouraged that the jeweler reiterated its full-year forecast despite expecting a soft first quarter. Tiffany's shares rose $1.32, or 1.9%, to trade at $69.23 in 4 p.m. trading Friday.
The company's Asian-Pacific region continued to be a stronghold, with sales rising 13% to $254 million in the fourth quarter. Openings of stores in China, Singapore and Australia assisted revenue growth.
Analysts applauded the jeweler's efforts in Asia. "It's a growing market and you aren't seeing momentum domestically or from Europe," said Leigh Drogen, chief executive of Estimize, which compiles analysts' estimates.
Total sales in the Americas rose 2% to $620 million. Sales at the New York flagship store, which makes up 8% of overall business, fell 3%. Total sales in Japan declined 6% to $192 million.
The company forecast fiscal 2014 earnings from operations of $3.43 to $3.53 a share on 6% to 8% sales growth. Analysts have projected $3.50 a share on a 6% revenue increase to $4.04 billion, according to a survey by Thomson Reuters.
Tiffany's "second half should be stronger than the first half as improved product innovation and marketing begins to take better hold," said Citigroup analyst Oliver Chen.
Tiffany warned that it expected fiscal-first-quarter adjusted earnings to decline about 15% to 20% because of gross margin pressure and higher marketing-related costs, while analysts were looking for flat profit. The company predicted earnings growth in subsequent quarters.
High-end shoppers have continued to snap up Tiffany's fine jewelry, such as canary-yellow diamonds and engagement rings.
But sales of silver jewelry -- which carry a higher profit margin than fine jewelry -- have declined of late as the retailer's less well-heeled customers have been affected by a weak economy, less-expensive knockoffs and what some people have considered a stagnant selection.
Tiffany has plans for an Art Deco collection of silver, onyx and freshwater pearls this spring, as a less-expensive complement to 1920s-style platinum and diamond jewelry it recently created. It also has been developing new products including a new metal alloy -- a mix of gold, silver and copper it calls Rubedo. Tiffany jewelry fashioned from the pink-hued metal start at $250.
For the quarter ended Jan. 31, Tiffany reported profit of $179.6 million, or $1.40 a share, up from $178.4 million, or $1.39 a share, a year earlier. Last year's earnings were $3.60 a share excluding costs to relocate Tiffany's New York headquarters staff.
The company's November projection was for earnings of $1.35 to $1.55 a share. In January Tiffany said it would come in at the bottom end.
Sales increased 4.1% to $1.24 billion, short of the $1.25 billion forecast by Wall Street. Excluding the effect of foreign-currency translation, sales rose 5%.
Same-store sales were flat.
---
Ann Zimmerman contributed to this article.

Owners Spar Over New York Landmark

Author: Karmin, Craig

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 23 Mar 2013: A.1.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/owners-spar-over-new-york-landmark/docview/1318889679/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: Mr. Malkin, 79, and his 50-year-old son, Anthony, have been trying for months to sell Mr. Kramer and about 2,800 other stakeholders on a sweeping deal to make the 102-story tower the centerpiece of a new public company traded on the New York Stock Exchange. In the 1990s, Japanese billionaire Hideki Yokoi bought the building, and his family recruited Donald Trump to lead an effort to break the long-term lease and seize control.\n

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Owners+Spar+Over+New+York+Landmark&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-23&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=A.1&amp;au=Karmin%2C+Craig&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Marshall Kramer, a 76-year-old retiree in Katy, Texas, picked up his phone recently and was surprised to hear the voice of Peter Malkin, whose family controls the Empire State Building.
Mr. Kramer and his two siblings own just one of the 3,300 shares in a private company that owns the famed skyscraper. Mr. Malkin was calling to persuade him to support the Malkin family's plan to take the company public. "I basically got a speech," recalls Mr. Kramer. "He sounded like a pushy salesman."
Mr. Malkin, 79, and his 50-year-old son, Anthony, have been trying for months to sell Mr. Kramer and about 2,800 other stakeholders on a sweeping deal to make the 102-story tower the centerpiece of a new public company traded on the New York Stock Exchange. It would be the second-largest IPO ever for a U.S. real-estate investment trust, or REIT, according to data provider Dealogic.
The Malkins need 80% support to proceed with the $1 billion offering. On Friday, they told owners they were extending the voting period, which could have closed on Monday. The Malkins said they may end voting when a New York State Court issues a ruling on one aspect of the plan, which is expected by May 2.
If the Malkins succeed, it will mark the end of a long and colorful era in the building's history that featured some of New York's best-known real-estate tycoons, a convoluted ownership structure and enough strife to keep lots of lawyers busy for years. The proposed deal was triggered by the 2007 death of Leona Helmsley, whose late husband, Harry, teamed up with Peter Malkin's father-in-law after the latter bought the building in 1961.
But first Anthony Malkin, who now runs the family company, must overcome resistance from some skeptical stakeholders -- many of whom inherited shares purchased a half-century ago from his grandfather, Lawrence Wien.
Mr. Kramer, for example, says he and his siblings got their ownership unit from their father, who told them he used to play gin rummy with Mr. Wien and was a friend of Harry Helmsley. Mr. Kramer says he recently voted "no" on the plan because he thinks it gives too big a share of the new company, which also will own 18 other Malkin properties, to the Malkin family and not enough to other stakeholders.
Anthony Malkin recently informed stakeholders that about 60% of the ownership units already had approved the plan. One supporter, Eli Mattioli, a lawyer who used to work with Mr. Wien, says the deal will bring the ownership structure "into the 21st century." Another, retiree Edward Bermas, says he thinks he'll make more money from the REIT. "I think the people who oppose it are more concerned with how much money other people are going to make," he says.
The proposed deal values the skyscraper itself at $2.3 billion, and the other 18 properties at $1.9 billion. The terms call for the Malkin family to own about 16.5% of the new Empire State Realty Trust, worth about $700 million. The deal values the Helmley estate's holdings at $1 billion; about two-thirds would be distributed as cash. The other Empire State Building stakeholders will own 24%, worth about $1 billion, and owners of the other properties will also get shares.
The Malkins have told stakeholders in writing that the proposed new ownership structure offers them fair value, and several advantages over the current structure. The new publicly traded shares, they say, will be more able to appreciate than units in the private company, for which there is no established trading market today. Investors who want to cash out can simply sell their shares. They also say the addition of the other buildings will make for a more diversified investment.
Currently, most units of the private company are worth about $323,000, according to the prospectus. Each year, those units receive a cash distribution based partly on whether the building's profit clears certain thresholds. Last year, the payout per unit was $5,199. The prospectus says that under the REIT structure, the comparable payout would be $5,866 in the first year.
The deal would do away with the final remnants of a Byzantine ownership and management structure that gave rise to years of feuding. After Mr. Wien bought the building in 1961, he set up a company to hold a lease on the entire building, selling stakes in that company -- the units now at issue -- for $10,000 apiece. Messrs. Wien and Helmsley set up another company to operate the building -- and share the profits. Then they resold the building itself to a big institutional investor.
In the 1990s, Japanese billionaire Hideki Yokoi bought the building, and his family recruited Donald Trump to lead an effort to break the long-term lease and seize control. At one point, Mr. Trump referred to the building as a "high-rise slum." Anthony Malkin and his father thwarted that effort.
Mr. Trump now is now complimentary of the Malkins, but characterizes the IPO plan as "a very complicated deal. Sounds to me like this is something that will end up in court, no matter what you do."
Separately, the Malkins were involved in litigation with Leona Helmsley -- nicknamed the "Queen of Mean" in New York -- and Helmsley-Spear Inc. over the contract to manage the building, a battle the Malkins won in 2006. The Malkins also arranged for the company holding the long-term lease to buy back the building from the Japanese ownership group.
Ms. Helmsley died in 2007. Her will stipulated that her interests in the Empire State Building should be liquidated.
Around that time, Anthony Malkin began overseeing a more than $550 million renovation of the building, which was erected in 1931 during the Great Depression, including restoring the Art Deco lobby and replacing all 6,514 windows. He also allowed leases to expire so he could combine spaces and attract higher-paying tenants. He lured Air China and French fragrance maker Coty, and social-networking company LinkedIn more than doubled its space.
The offering prospectus doesn't disclose past performance but projects the skyscraper's net operating income will increase from $84.3 million in the fiscal year ending June 2013 to $135.9 million for the year ending June 2015.
The Malkins have spent much of the last year trying to drum up support for the IPO plan.
Howard Peskoe, a New York lawyer, says he and his wife voted "yes." He cites the ability to trade the new shares and cash out after years of holding an illiquid asset. "The Empire State Building is a magical place, but it was a second-rate property," Mr. Peskoe says. "The Malkins brought it up to modern standards."
If Mr. Malkin doesn't secure the necessary votes, he can push back the voting deadline to as late as the end of 2014 as he negotiates with holdouts.
For months, the plan's detractors have been raising questions about terms of the deal, from whether the Malkins are shortchanging other owners to the tax ramifications to stakeholders. Last year, the Malkins settled a lawsuit brought by stakeholders over terms of the deal. The case now before the New York court is over a challenge to one aspect of the voting procedure.
Some of the criticisms have gotten personal. "Tony [Malkin] treats the Empire State Building like it's his property and we are just another piece of it," complains stakeholder Andrew Shact, whose says he grandfather was on social terms with Mr. Wien. Mr. Shact says he voted "no."
Anthony Malkin has said to investors that his critics are misinformed about details in the plan and are confusing other owners with misrepresentations.
Robert Machleder, a stakeholder and former law partner of Mr. Wien, says he called Peter Malkin last month to object to a stipulation in the IPO plan that awards $300 million to the Malkins as part of profit-sharing arrangement related to the Empire State Building and the other properties.
Mr. Machleder says he told Mr. Malkin he was going to share his thoughts with other owners. He says he was taken aback when the Malkins sent out a letter, labeled "Misinformation Alert," that defended the $300 million and seemed to cast doubt on Mr. Machleder's motives. "Certain individuals have intentionally waited until the last minute, in some cases for years, to attempt to disrupt your vote," the letter said.
Carol Green is a retiree who owns two units. "As the Empire State Building gets better, it's going to earn more," she says, which would mean that her payouts would go up under the current arrangement. She says uncertainty about what will happen to the value of a public stock caused her to vote "no."
"I don't know if the REIT is going to go up," she says.

China's Box Office Tally: $2.7 Billion

Author: Fritz, Ben

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 22 Mar 2013: B.6.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/chinas-box-office-tally-2-7-billion/docview/1318674075/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: On a conference call with reporters, MPAA Chief Executive Chris Dodd said such issues are "still a concern" and that his Hollywood studio trade group has "raised our concerns about that with the very highest authorities we have access to."

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=China%27s+Box+Office+Tally%3A+%242.7+Billion&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-22&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=B.6&amp;au=Fritz%2C+Ben&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   China surpassed Japan in 2012 to become the world's second-largest movie market, behind the U.S., with box-office receipts in the world's most populous nation up 36% to $2.7 billion.
The new data, contained in a report released Thursday by the Motion Picture Association of America, underscores the growing importance of China to Hollywood's studios despite the ongoing challenges they face in exporting their movies there.
Last year, concerned that foreign films were taking too big a share of box office, the government-controlled China Film distribution company released some big Hollywood movies on the same date, limiting their commercial potential.
Among the blockbusters pitted against each other were "The Dark Knight Rises," from Time Warner Inc.'s Warner Bros. and Sony Pictures Entertainment's "The Amazing Spider-Man."
In the U.S., those films opened more than two weeks apart. China Film also imposed several "blackout periods" during which no foreign films were allowed to play in theaters.
On a conference call with reporters, MPAA Chief Executive Chris Dodd said such issues are "still a concern" and that his Hollywood studio trade group has "raised our concerns about that with the very highest authorities we have access to."
China enjoyed the fastest growth of the world's top 10 movie markets, an MPAA spokesman said. Total global box office rose 6% to $34.7 billion, thanks to increases Latin America, North America and the Asia Pacific region.
But declines in France, Italy, Spain and other countries hurt receipts in Europe, the Middle East and Africa, which fell 1% to $10.7 billion.
Box-office receipts in the U.S. and Canada rose 6% to $10.8 billion, as 1.36 billion tickets were sold, 80 million more than in 2011. The average ticket price rose less than 1% to $7.96, after at least nine years of steeper price hikes. Admissions fell in both 2010 and 2011, and are down more than 10% since 2003.
Last year's positive news hasn't continued so far this year, however, as flops like "Jack the Giant Slayer" and Arnold Schwarzenegger's "The Last Stand" have helped to drive domestic receipts down 12% so far compared with the same period in 2012.
John Fithian, CEO of the National Association of Theater Owners, blamed the decline on a lack of diversity in the offerings from studios, saying there have been too many R-rated movies. Based on the films planned for future release, he said he expects that negative trend to turn around by the end of 2013.

MANSION --- Rock-Solid Decor --- Advances in concrete lead to furnishings with an organic look and a smooth finish

Author: Buerger, Megan

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 22 Mar 2013: M.4.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/mansion-rock-solid-decor-advances-concrete-lead/docview/1318673644/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: Certain mixes produce a thinner and lighter product than traditional concrete, allowing designers to venture beyond countertops and flooring to smaller furniture pieces such as coffee tables and lounge chairs.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=MANSION+---+Rock-Solid+Decor+---+Advances+in+concrete+lead+to+furnishings+with+an+organic+look+and+a+smooth+finish&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-22&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=M.4&amp;au=Buerger%2C+Megan&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Concrete has gone far beyond sidewalks and fallout shelters, and now it's increasingly popular in home decor. "People are becoming more attracted to concrete, and I think it has a lot to do with the possibilities it offers," said John Strieder, editor in chief of Concrete Decor Magazine, which started in 2001.
Manufacturers and artists are experimenting with engineered mixes, swapping aggregate materials for fiberglass and polymer and adding colors and textures, Mr. Strieder said. Certain mixes produce a thinner and lighter product than traditional concrete, allowing designers to venture beyond countertops and flooring to smaller furniture pieces such as coffee tables and lounge chairs.
Last week, around 2,000 architects, retailers and curious homeowners gathered in Charlotte, N.C., for the fourth-annual Concrete Decor Show, which showcases the newest technology and products in the industry. Here are some concrete examples.
GAME ON
James DeWulf, a 37-year-old Los Angeles designer, was turned on to concrete after seeing someone build prison beds at a concrete shop in 2004. Today, he's best known for his concrete ping-pong table, which sells for $7,000. Mr. DeWulf, who owns James DeWulf LLC, recently designed a pool table, which costs $16,000 for the indoor version and $18,000 for the outdoor version. Concrete has become a more acceptable furniture material, Mr. DeWulf said, because advances in the material have made it lighter, stronger and more stain resistant. "And ours has this beautiful, buttery finish. At trade shows, everyone that walks by runs their fingers across the table."
CLIMBING THE WALLS
While most of its clients are universities and sports centers, it's not unusual for Entre-Prises Climbing Walls to get requests for residential projects. "Rock-climbers are pretty passionate, and many are looking for that natural-stone look," said Jason Stollenwerk, who manages the U.S. operations in Oregon for Entre-Prises, which also has offices in France, England, Germany, Spain and China. The company offers a range of products, from 4-by-4-foot panels for $400 that clients can self-install, to custom interior projects that cost upward of $100,000. They even have a product that looks like ice. "It's a dense material that you can actually use ice-climbing tools on," he said, "for the die-hards."
TRIAL BY FIRE
As concrete cements its place in the high-end-decor market, it has also become a thrifty alternative to pricier stones such as limestone and marble. Scott Sterling, who runs a pre-cast concrete business in Santa Ana, Calif., said many of his clients seek out concrete because it's cheaper. "A fancy limestone fireplace will be tens of thousands of dollars," he said. "We make some really cool fireplaces that look like stone but cost $2,500." Including installation, fireplaces cost around $4,000. Moldings for doors and windows cost $10 to $12 per linear foot.
CEMENT CELLAR
At his Brooklyn studio, Chris Oricchio builds industrial-style decor such as barnwood pot racks ($200), concrete dining tables ($1,400) and travertine and mahogany coffee tables ($850). But wine bunkers, which cost $25 a unit, are his best sellers. Made of plaster and concrete cast into wood, the modular bunkers have rough, intentionally imperfect edges. "Concrete is like silly putty," said Mr. Oricchio, the 32-year-old owner of Decor Atelier. "It picks up the scarifications of whatever you cast it on, and that's what makes it beautiful."
HOB KNOBING
Grey Hensey, a 22-year-old design student at Auburn University and founder of Kast Concrete, has carved out a career niche with his concrete knobs ($8 each). He casts concrete into rubber molds, for a smooth, porcelainlike finish. "Everyone is using raw materials like metal, wood and concrete," Mr. Hensey said, "but by creating a glassy look, I'm trying to expand people's perceptions of what concrete can be. It doesn't have to look like a sidewalk, it can be delicate and refined."
LEFT HANGING
Kyle Bragg, a 28-year-old architect in Louisville, Ky., was inspired by the creative ways concrete was being used in large building projects and saw potential in its versatility. "It can be clean and modern with flat surfaces and hard corners," he said, "but it also has a wonderful rustic nature, with minor imperfections that make each piece unique." He launched FormdDesign in 2010 and sells his products at local stores around Louisville, but most of his business is online through Etsy, a site for artists and crafting. The wall hooks, his most popular item, are $27 for a set of three.

Suntech Rattles Investors in U.S.

Author: Ma, Wayne; Glazer, Emily

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 21 Mar 2013: B.5.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/suntech-rattles-investors-u-s/docview/1318207328/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: The Chinese banks are owed as much as 7.1 billion yuan ($1.14 billion) and include Industrial & Commercial Bank of China Ltd., Agricultural Bank of China and Bank of China Ltd., the state-run Xinhua news agency reported. [...]its earnings have declined because of a global oversupply of solar panels, a drop in prices and antidumping tariffs imposed on China by the U.S. that have weighed on the industry generally.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Suntech+Rattles+Investors+in+U.S.&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-03-21&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=B.5&amp;au=Ma%2C+Wayne%3BGlazer%2C+Emily&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Solar-panel maker Suntech Power Holdings Co. has been forced into Chinese bankruptcy proceedings, sparking questions about how U.S. investors will fare in the decline of one of China's most prominent companies.
Given Suntech's status as a major employer and a key player in an emerging industry -- it once was the world's largest supplier of solar panels -- Chinese authorities might be reluctant to let the company fold.
But if Suntech is liquidated, its Chinese creditors, who are owed more than $2 billion, likely would gain access to the company's assets before foreign bondholders would.
U.S. creditors were gearing up for a fight Wednesday. Suntech defaulted on a $541 million U.S. bond payment on Friday.
"If they take all the assets and give nothing to the U.S. investors, on the next deal, that's going to be remembered," said James Millar. The Wilmer Cutler Pickering Hale and Dorr LLP partner represents four bondholders that had threatened to sue the company in the U.S. to collect on their investment after Suntech defaulted on the bond payment.
Mr. Millar said Wednesday that he and his clients were trying to determine if U.S. bondholders would get a seat in negotiations in China. Advisers for other bondholders declined to comment or couldn't be reached.
Suntech's bankruptcy also threatened to ripple beyond the company's stakeholders after corporate accounting scandals and a slowdown in the world's second-largest economy have rattled U.S. investors once enamored with China.
"Suntech was quite a highflier, and being able to list in the U.S. was a big deal," said Joseph Chan, a Shanghai-based partner at law firm Sidley Austin LLP. "Now the poster child is gone."
Himanshu Shah, president of Shah Capital Management, said his firm exited roughly a $4 million stake in Suntech in early January.
"There are always risks involved in investing anywhere, including China, so as an investor you have to do your due diligence better," said Mr. Shah. His firm has about $200 million in assets, including some Chinese companies, he said. "You really have to look at the shareholder and ownership structure." Most of Suntech's assets were pledged to Chinese lenders, which gave foreign lenders less leverage and protection, he said.
Mr. Shah said Suntech's bankruptcy could help healthy players in the industry capture a bigger share of the market. His firm has stakes in Suntech competitors Yingli Green Energy Holding Co., Trina Solar Ltd. and Canadian Solar Inc.
Suntech said Wednesday that eight Chinese banks on Monday filed an involuntary petition for insolvency and restructuring of the company's main operating subsidiary in China. The subsidiary, Wuxi Suntech, won't file an objection to the petition, Suntech said.
The Wuxi Municipal Intermediate People's Court in Jiangsu province will decide whether to accept the petition in the next few days, Suntech said. If the petition is approved, Suntech would continue to produce solar products to meet customer orders, the company said.
The Chinese banks are owed as much as 7.1 billion yuan ($1.14 billion) and include Industrial & Commercial Bank of China Ltd., Agricultural Bank of China and Bank of China Ltd., the state-run Xinhua news agency reported.
The default on the $541 million U.S. bond triggered cross-defaults for Suntech's other outstanding debt, the company said.
Several Chinese companies in recent years have defaulted on bonds issued overseas, with mixed results for investors.
Suntech issued its bonds through a Cayman holding company in 2008, forcing creditors to go through court proceedings in that jurisdiction. Although 60% of Suntech bondholders have said they are willing to defer payment for two months, the remaining 40% still could try to force it to declare bankruptcy in the U.S. Such a filing would be the first of its kind in the U.S. for such a large Chinese company, but it wasn't clear that would be allowed under U.S. law.
"Investors need to know that when buying bonds from the Cayman holding company of a Chinese firm, they don't have recourse over the mainland assets," said Neil McDonald, a lawyer in Hong Kong at Hogan Lovells who specializes in corporate restructuring.
Wuxi-based Suntech remains one of the world's largest solar-panel manufacturers. But its earnings have declined because of a global oversupply of solar panels, a drop in prices and antidumping tariffs imposed on China by the U.S. that have weighed on the industry generally. The company said recently that it would end production at its plant in Arizona next month.
Suntech has been trying to find a white knight to take over and inject capital into the company. On Tuesday Suntech appointed two board members, one of whom is a former executive at Wuxi Goulian Development Corp., a state-backed investment firm.
The solar industry's debt deepened between 2009 and 2011 to fund expansion of manufacturing capacity. But while global solar-power demand has grown each year, it hasn't kept pace with manufacturing.
China had continued to support its solar companies, even as U.S. and European manufacturers had been forced into restructuring or bankruptcy. But China's State Council, the country's cabinet, in December signaled it would stop funding unprofitable domestic solar-panel makers and instead encourage mergers among healthy companies.
---
Dinny McMahon, Kathy Chu and Grace Zhu contributed to this article.
