Credit: By Spencer Jakab

Subject: Earnings forecasting; Fast food industry; Earnings per share; Fast food

Business indexing term: Subject: Earnings forecasting Fast food industry Earnings per share; Industry: 72251 :‎ Restaurants and Other Eating Places

Full text:   LOT POLISH AIRLINES
Poland May Reallocate
All of Carrier's Assets
The Polish government is considering stripping its troubled LOT Polish Airlines of all assets and moving them to a smaller airline that it controls, a person familiar with the matter said Monday, a transition intended to salvage LOT's historic name.
The loss-making LOT in December requested state aid as passenger numbers fell drastically in the second half of 2012. It received $127 million in an emergency loan for six months from the state. The European Commission could rule that this form of public aid distorts competition, which would force LOT to return the funds and likely result in its uncontrolled bankruptcy.
The government, which holds 93% of LOT and 62% of smaller peer Eurolot, said in January that LOT would have to restructure and shrink by nearly a half, with Eurolot taking over domestic and European flights and LOT left to operate routes to the U.S. and Asia. A more radical solution, with Eurolot filling in for LOT on all destinations, could offer a permanent fix. This would allow the LOT brand to continue under the operations of Eurolot without the heavy baggage of debts and staff redundancy negotiations with trade unions.
-- Marcin Sobczyk
---
GLENCORE
Merger With Xstrata
Clears More Hurdles
South Africa's Competition Tribunal said Friday that hearings on the proposed merger between Glencore International PLC and Xstrata PLC have ended after South Africa's state utility Eskom and labor unions withdrew complaints.
The Tribunal now has 10 days to deliver a ruling on the merger deal, Tribunal spokeswoman Nandi Mokoena said. The ruling still could result in conditions being imposed upon the merger, she added.
The announcement removes some of the last few hurdles in the two companies' quest to create the world's fourth-largest diversified miner, with a market capitalization of about $80 billion. Glencore and Xstrata already have secured the backing of their shareholders and the European Union, but are waiting for approval from competition authorities in South Africa and China.
The two companies also said Friday they have agreed to extend the legal deadline for their merger by six weeks to March 15, to provide more time to secure those approvals.
-- Alex MacDonald and Devon Maylie
---
TOTAL SA
Oil Company Keeps Uganda
Exploration License
France's Total SA is set to retain a major oil license in the northern section of Uganda's Lake Albertine Rift basin, thanks to a discovery late last month, company and government officials said.
The discovery -- after months of extensive drilling activity -- is a major boost for Total, whose exploration license for that block, known as 1A, was due to expire in February.
Honey Malinga, the assistant commissioner at Uganda's state-run Petroleum Exploration and Production Department, said the discovery would boost the size of the country's crude reserves, currently estimated at 3.5 billion barrels.
"Total will automatically retain the license," Mr. Malinga said. "We have asked them to apply for an appraisal and production license for the block."
Company spokesman Florent Segura said the discovery requires further appraisal to determine its potential. "Total confirms the discovery of hydrocarbons during the drilling of the exploration well Lyec-1 [in block 1A]," he said in an emailed statement, adding that the company has "asked the authorities to renew the license so that we can continue our exploration program."
-- Nicholas Bariyo
---
SCHLUMBERGER
Oil-Field Company's
4th-Quarter Profit Falls
Schlumberger Ltd.'s fourth-quarter earnings fell 3.7% amid lower revenue from its international operations and a slowdown in North American onshore activity.
However, a strong offshore performance helped soften the blow.
The world's largest oil-field-services company earns more than two-thirds of its revenue internationally, which had insulated it from a downturn in North American activity during the first part of 2012. But the company warned last month that its fourth-quarter earnings would take a hit from weaker-than-expected North America activity and delays in Europe, the former Soviet republics and Africa.
Schlumberger reported a fourth-quarter profit of $1.36 billion, or $1.02 a share, down from $1.41 billion, or $1.05 a share, in the same period a year earlier. But excluding items such as merger and integration costs, the company beat analysts' expectations with per-share earnings from continuing operations of $1.08, down from $1.10 a year earlier. Revenue jumped 8.5% to $11.17 billion.
-- Alison Sider and Melodie Warner

Global Finance: China Stocks Turn Inside Out --- As Domestic Investors Flee Languid Markets, Eager Foreigners Are Being Wooed

Author: Gu, Wei

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]. 22 Jan 2013: C.3.

https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/global-finance-china-stocks-turn-inside-out-as/docview/1271849954/se-2?accountid=14426

Abstract: Just one-third of Chinese brokerage accounts hold stocks, an all-time low, according to China Securities Depositary and Clearing Corp., which manages clearing and settlement for China's stock markets.

Links: http://www.yidu.edu.cn/educhina/educhina.do?artifact=&amp;svalue=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;stype=2&amp;s=on

http://pqdt.calis.edu.cn/SearchResults.aspx?pm=0&amp;q=

http://159.226.100.141/Reader/union_result.jsp?title=1&amp;word=Wall+Street+Journal

https://tsinghua-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com.cn/openurl/86THU/86THU?url_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;genre=article&amp;sid=ProQ:ProQ%3Aabiglobal&amp;atitle=Global+Finance%3A+China+Stocks+Turn+Inside+Out+---+As+Domestic+Investors+Flee+Languid+Markets%2C+Eager+Foreigners+Are+Being+Wooed&amp;title=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;issn=00999660&amp;date=2013-01-22&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=C.3&amp;au=Gu%2C+Wei&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;rft_id=info:eric/&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Full text:   Foreign buyers are now being seen as the potential salvation for a Chinese stock market bereft of domestic investors, who have turned their sights to stocks abroad.
China's markets were among the worst performers globally last year, and have performed poorly for the past five years even as other markets have doubled.
Just one-third of Chinese brokerage accounts hold stocks, an all-time low, according to China Securities Depositary and Clearing Corp., which manages clearing and settlement for China's stock markets. Instead, investors are embracing a program that allows them to invest overseas.
Last year marked the biggest increase in quotas for a program known as QDII, for Qualified Domestic Institutional Investors, putting the total since its inauguration in 2007 at $86 billion.
"I don't want to put all my eggs in the same China basket," said Dora Tao, an accountant in Shanghai who is considering investing in the QDII program.
But where Chinese are ignoring their local market, foreign investors see bargains and are maxing out on the quotas that allow them to invest in Chinese stocks that trade in the mainland.
Now China's top securities regulator has said that quotas that allow foreigners to invest in Chinese equity markets could be increased tenfold.
"The five brokers we work with don't have any more quota left for us; everyone is looking to get new quotas," said Aaron Boesky, chief executive of Marco Polo Investments Group. which focuses on mainland Chinese stocks. "Foreign investors who haven't been through those terrible years see China now as a great buying opportunity."
As part of its effort to boost its market, China is expanding those quotas to an eager audience.
That program is known as QFII, for Qualified Foreign Institutional Investors, and allows investment funds, endowments and the like to invest in Chinese stocks that trade on the Shanghai and Shenzhen exchanges.
It took China a decade to issue $36 billion in quotas for foreign investors, about a day's worth of combined trading volume for the mainland markets.
Then last April, the country's securities regulator more than doubled QFII quotas to $80 billion, and in December it decided to lift a cap for sovereign-wealth funds and central banks that prevented a single institution from investing more than $1 billion.
With a new program that allows Chinese brokers to get overseas yuan back into the Chinese markets, equities could see up to $70 billion in new foreign money, which equals 5% of the free float of Chinese stocks, Mr. Boesky said.
But foreigners seem to be the only ones who are eager to get into the Chinese market because, unlike the Chinese investors, they haven't experienced the five-year bear market.
Like investors everywhere, Chinese tend to buy the investments with the best recent track record. That is one reason they are putting money overseas.
For the past two years, funds investing overseas have handily beaten the funds that invest inside China. In 2012, funds that let Chinese invest abroad were up an average of 10%, with the top performer up 30%, while the Shanghai stock market was up only slightly.
The Chinese government started the QDII program just as the financial crisis was about to hit, so the inaugural performance was rather inauspicious.
The first four funds fell by as much as 40% and frustrated investors responded by dumping their holdings.
Better subsequent performance and encouragement by the Chinese government -- which is pushing residents to venture abroad to help lower price pressures inside the country on everything from paintings to properties -- have drawn investors back into the funds.
China's central bank said in early January that it would study the possibility of starting a second program, which would allow domestic investors to invest in overseas stocks directly.
Chinese funds that invest abroad often focus on well-known overseas-listed Chinese companies, including Internet darlings such as Baidu Inc. and Tencent Holdings Ltd. By doing so, they have managed to avoid damage from the accounting blowups that have plagued some Chinese stocks.
The improving performance of funds that invest abroad has helped bring in more assets. Two-thirds of the 70-some QDII funds were opened in the past two years.
"Chinese investors have gone out of the initial panic stage after the global financial crisis," said Ding Chen, chief executive of CSOP Asset Management. "The sentiment towards overseas investing has turned."
The best performing QDII fund in the past six months is Fortune SG Fund Management's China growth fund, which rose 30% by investing in Hong Kong and U.S.-listed Chinese companies. Luxury goods, emerging markets, properties and commodities also have been popular.
